**Set-aside reasons** (76 rows):

- (1) ra.ad meaning physical earth-trembling at divine presence, a cosmic natural even
- (1) yir.ah meaning practical avoidance of physical hazard (briers and thorns), not i
- (1) yir.ah used adjectivally to describe the visual quality of wheel rims, not an in
- (1) me.gu.rah used as 'granary/barn' (storage place for seed), not as fear or dread
- (1) ra.gaz meaning to quarrel or be agitated with each other in a social context, no
- (1) ra.gaz meaning literal earthquake/seismic quaking of the earth, a physical cosmi
- (1) ra.gaz meaning cosmic/physical trembling of heavenly foundations during theophan
- (1) ra.gaz meaning raging arrogance/fury directed outward against God, not inner fea
- (1) ra.gaz meaning raging aggression/fury against God, not inner fear or terror — ou
- (1) ra.gaz meaning physical trembling of the earth's pillars under divine power, a c
- (1) ra.gaz meaning to provoke/challenge God in an outward relational sense, not inne
- (1) ra.gaz meaning cosmic/physical trembling of mountain foundations in theophany, n
- (1) ra.gaz meaning physical trembling of the earth in a storm theophany, not inner h
- (1) ra.gaz meaning outward raging/angry agitation of a fool in argument, not inner f
- (1) ra.gaz meaning figurative earth-trembling as social/cosmic disruption metaphor,

<a id="s2"></a>
## §2. Verses by sub-group

All verses for cluster terms, grouped by the analytical sub-group the term belongs to. Within each sub-group the rows are sorted canonically (book · chapter · verse). The **Term** column shows the Strong's number and transliteration of the cluster term whose `wa_verse_records` row generated this entry; **Spans in verse** lists every term-span recorded at that verse location.

Status precedence: G = group-assigned (analysed) · SA = set-aside · NR = is_relevant=0 · P = pending in VC · UT = untouched (no VC row).

**ID columns:** `vr_id` is `wa_verse_records.id`; `mti_id` is `mti_terms.id` (also `wa_verse_records.mti_term_id` and `verse_context.mti_term_id`). Both are exposed so AI can author VCREVISE / VCNEW / VCVERSE patches directly from this report — no separate ID-resolver query needed. The `(vr_id, mti_id)` pair is the natural key for any `verse_context` operation.

<a id="s2-1"></a>
### §2.1 _(unrouted / unassigned)_

_Verses whose `verse_context.cluster_subgroup_id` is NULL, or whose term has no `mti_term_subgroup` mapping._

## §3. Per-term comprehensive detail

Each term gets numbered sections: identity • meaning • anchor-verse linkages • groups • findings • pointers • auxiliary data. Verses are not repeated here — they are listed by sub-group in §2. Items linked only by registry are summarised here; exhaustive lists are in the appendix §4.

---

<a id="t-H3372G"></a>
### H3372G ya.re — to fear: revere (`mti_id=298`)

**Identity & meaning**

1. Strong's: `H3372G` · Lang: Hebrew · Owner: OWNER
2. Registry: R061 fear · Legacy C-cluster: C06
3. Sub-group: —
4. Term status: extracted · Evidential: — · Occurrences: 208
5. Patch-authoring refs: `mti_id=298` · `md_version=2` · `vc_status=vc_completed`

**Verses:** 194 distinct locations (see §2 for the verse table grouped by sub-group).

**Group memberships (3)**

| Group ID | Code | Description | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| 927 | 298-001 | Term names divine command not to fear — the divine assurance 'Fear not / Do not be afraid' addressed to individuals in crisis, granting inner peace through the declaration of divine presence |  |
| 928 | 298-002 | Term names the reverential fear of the Lord as the proper inner orientation — fearing God rather than humans as the inner disposition of covenant loyalty, worship, and moral conduct |  |
| 929 | 298-003 | Term names the practical inner fear of threatening powers — the inner condition of dread before enemies, authorities, or circumstances that threaten life or wellbeing |  |

**Findings — direct (Strong's mention) (1)**

| Finding ID | Type | Anchor verses | Excerpt |
|---|---|---|---|
| DIM-61-002 | DIMENSION_REVIEW |  | ya.re (H3372G) groups add the divine 'Fear not' command (298-001) as a structuring element — showing the divine address to inner fear as a distinct inner-being category. The reassurance pattern (divine declaration of presence + commanded displacement of fear) is significant for understanding how the inner-being state of fear is meant to be transformed. |

**Findings — via anchor verse (22 unique)**

| Finding ID | Type | Matched anchor refs | Excerpt |
|---|---|---|---|
| DIM-19-001 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | Isa 43:1 | The calling registry (Reg 19) has 13 of 24 groups (54%) assigned Divine-Human Correspondence — the highest concentration of any single registry in the programme to date. The calling vocabulary is structurally a divine-human act: God calls, names, and constitutes; the human receives, responds, and is formed. Session B should examine how the human inner person is changed by the divine call, and what distinguishes the groups where HUMAN volition or emotion is the primary inner-being phenomenon from those where the divine calling act is the governing feature. |
| OBS-034-T2-063 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | 2Ki 17:38 | Covenant structures and disciplines memory — it does not bypass it. (1) Covenant enables and deepens memory in those who maintain it: the covenantal commands to remember (Deu 4:23; 8:18) orient the inner memory faculty toward God's acts and commitments. The covenant creates a framework within which memory is directed and disciplined — festivals, signs (rainbow, circumcision, Sabbath, Eucharist), and written law all serve as memory aids that structure the inner faculty's operation. (2) Covenant breach is associated with forgetting: "Take care, lest you forget the covenant" — the drift from covenant faithfulness begins in the memory faculty's failure to hold covenantal reality. The covenant-breaker is characterised by forgetting God's covenant (2Ki 17:38: "you shall not forget the covenant that I have made with you"). (3) The new covenant does not abolish the memory structure but reorients it: the Eucharistic "do this in remembrance of me" establishes a covenantal memory practice centred on Christ's death rather than Sinai's law-giving. Memory is retained and redirected, not bypassed. |
| OBS-099-T2-021 | OBSERVATION | Psa 23:4 | Yes — three contextual variations: (a) Divine vs. human scope: God's chesed inexhaustible; human chesed creaturely and can be withdrawn [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-083, Q&A-008]. (b) Comfort vs. affliction: Job 6:4 (afflicting presence) vs. Psa 23:4 (comforting presence) — same term, different mode by context and divine purpose [OBS-099-067/066]. (c) Purposive vs. sustaining: Rom 2:4 — kindness aimed at repentance; Luke 6:35 — kindness to ungrateful without stated aim [OBS-099-076, OBS-099-078]. Purposive dimension present in some contexts; absent as explicit feature in others. |
| OBS-099-T2-023 | OBSERVATION | Psa 23:4 | Two responses evidenced: (a) Praise — Psa 63:3 — the immediate response to God's chesed is praise and upward orientation [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-084]. (b) Relief from fear — Psa 23:4 — divine presence displaces fear [OBS-099-066]. Gap: the evidence does not directly address the immediate response to received human kindness. Divine reception is better evidenced than human-to-human reception. |
| OBS-099-T2-024 | OBSERVATION | Psa 23:4 | Not fully consistent across contexts. Praise (Psa 63:3), relief from fear (Psa 23:4), and petition (Psa 86:5 — "show me your steadfast love" [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-089]) are all evidenced. The variation is contextual (posture of recipient: faithful, in need, or in crisis) rather than contradictory. |
| OBS-099-T2-028 | OBSERVATION | Psa 23:4 | Two conditions evidenced: (a) Trust/dependence — Gen 28:20 (Jacob's vow) and Psa 23:4 show reception is enabled by dependence and trust [OBS-099-065/066]. The creature who acknowledges its creatureliness receives divine accompaniment as kindness. (b) Covenant orientation — Exo 20:6 / Deu 7:9 — God shows chesed to those who love him and keep his commandments [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-089]. Orientation, not merit, is the condition. Gap: Luke 6:35 shows chesed reaching the ungrateful and evil [OBS-099-078] — suggesting initial encounter conditions may differ from sustained formation conditions. |
| OBS-099-T2-054 | OBSERVATION | Psa 23:4 | Kindness is one of the primary characteristics that builds and sustains relational connection — it constitutes relationships in their quality, not merely accompanies them. Chesed is the inner substance of covenant relationship [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-083]. The im.ma.di groups frame kindness as the quality making relational presence real rather than nominal [OBS-099-065–071]. 1Sa 20:14 — request for relational faithfulness to be maintained into the future [OBS-099-070]. The chasid's relational quality is his defining identity before God and others [XREG: H2623, OBS-099-094]. The person without kindness has relationships in form but not in substance. |
| OBS-099-T2-055 | OBSERVATION | Psa 23:4 | Most extensively evidenced direction in the registry. H2617A group 536-001 (180 relevant verses, dominant subject GOD [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-083]) documents the full range. (a) How: specific historical acts (Exo 15:13; 2Sa 7:15 [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-089]); through his presence (Psa 23:4 [OBS-099-066]); through forgiveness (Exo 34:6–7); eschatologically through Christ (Eph 2:7 [XREG: G5544, OBS-099-093]). (b) Basis: covenantal (to those who love him — Exo 20:6) and unconditional in ultimate attribute (never ceases — Lam 3:22 [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-085]; reaches ungrateful — Luke 6:35 [OBS-099-078]). Conditionality is in manifestation; attribute itself is unconditional. (c) What it reveals: God whose primary inner disposition toward the creature is committed faithful generous good will — chesed before, through, and after judgment. |
| OBS-099-T2-063 | OBSERVATION | Psa 23:4 | Yes — rich evidence. (a) Divine kindness as response to suffering: Psa 23:4 (presence in death's valley), Lam 3:22 (chesed that does not cease through Jerusalem's destruction), Psa 94:18 ("when I thought my foot slips, your steadfast love held me up") [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-089, OBS-099-066]. (b) Kindness tested through suffering: Job 6:4/9:35 — divine presence as afflicting [OBS-099-067/068]; Job 10:12 — care preserving spirit through suffering [OBS-099-067 context]. Reveals that kindness is not only comforting face but refining face of divine presence. (c) Sacrificial solidarity: Gen 44:29/32 — Jacob's grief and Judah's surety-burden show the giver bears suffering on behalf of the recipient [OBS-099-062/063]. Suffering does not impair kindness; it may deepen and reveal it. |
| OBS-099-T2-076 | OBSERVATION | Psa 23:4 | (P1 — most useful framework) Moral philosophy and developmental psychology. Moral philosophy: kindness as other-oriented virtue — but chesed exceeds Aristotelian beneficence: it is covenantally obligated and divinely grounded, not merely virtuous. Developmental psychology: the chasid formation arc describes a developmental trajectory — character formed over time through relational encounters and deliberate practice [XREG: H2623, OBS-099-094]. (P2 — illumination) Attachment theory illuminates the chesed relationship: God's chesed as secure attachment base (Psa 23:4 — "you are with me" as the secure base from which the person faces the valley of death [OBS-099-066]). The chasid is the person with secure attachment to God, expressed in relational capacity toward others. Makes the evidence more coherent. (P3 — divergence) Biblical chesed exceeds psychological attachment: it is not merely emotional security but covenantal obligation and moral formation. Psychology can describe the attachment function; it cannot account for the covenantal structure. (P4 — gaps) Evidence does not address formation of kindness in early development or parental kindness shaping child's capacity for chesed. A genuine gap requiring further verse investigation. |
| OBS-099-T2-081 | OBSERVATION | Psa 23:4 | Yes — and substantively. The evidence shows kindness engaging the affective faculty in multiple directions. (a) Receiving divine chesed produces affective states: Psa 63:3 — "your steadfast love is better than life; my lips will praise you" — the receipt of divine chesed generates an affective orientation of praise and joy [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-084]. Psa 23:4 — "I will fear no evil, for you are with me" — the displacement of fear by security is an affective change produced by the experience of divine kindness-as-presence [OBS-099-066]. (b) Kindness involves an affective orientation in the giver: Eph 4:32 — "tenderhearted" (eusplanchnoi — literally "good-bowelled," an affective visceral term) is placed immediately alongside kindness, suggesting that genuine kindness carries an affective warmth component — it does not operate as cold duty [OBS-099-077]. (c) The absence of kindness produces grief: Gen 44:29 — Jacob's anticipatory grief at losing Benjamin — the possibility of losing the object of kindness generates profound affective distress [OBS-099-062]. The affective faculty is engaged at all three interfaces: receiving kindness (produces joy/security), giving kindness (accompanied by tenderheartedness), and threatened absence of kindness (produces grief/distress). |
| OBS-117-T2-023 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Judg 6:23 | The immediate responses to shalom's presence documented in the data: (1) Rest and sleep — Psa 4:8 ("in peace I will both lie down and sleep"); shalom immediately enables the cessation of vigilance; (2) Absence of fear — Judg 6:23 ("Peace be to you. Do not fear") — OBS-117-144; the divine peace immediately displaces terror; (3) Gladness and praise — Psa 35:27 ("shout for joy and be glad... Great is the Lord, who delights in the welfare of his servant") — OBS-117-149; shalom's presence triggers praise; (4) Heart-joining — 1Ch 12:17 ("my heart will be joined to you") — OBS-117-151; shalom's presence in friendship produces heart-union; (5) Daniel's strengthening — Dan 10:19 ("peace be with you; be strong and of good courage") — the angelic peace immediately produces inner strength. The pattern: shalom's immediate effect is the displacement of its contraries (fear, vigilance, inner fragmentation) and the enabling of their alternatives (rest, praise, courage, heart-union). |
| OBS-117-T2-066 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Jer 30:10 | Yes — extensively. Peace is itself primarily an experiential/affective condition in many of its manifestations. The Emotion-Positive dimension assignments (groups 2508-001, 2509-001, 419-002, 418-004, 2585-001, 2585-002, and others) directly name the affective dimension. Key affective evidence: Psa 4:8 — lying down and sleeping in peace (the affect of deep security); Psa 35:27 — shout for joy and be glad, because of the Lord's delight in welfare (joy triggered by shalom); Jer 30:10 — "Jacob shall return and have quiet and ease, and none shall make him afraid" — ease as the affective state of the peacefully restored. The affect-peace connection is foundational: peace is, at the affective level, the felt condition of security, rest, welfare, and the absence of fear. |
| OBS-117-T2-067 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Judg 6:23 | Peace enables positive affect and resolves negative affect. Evidence: (1) Judg 6:23 — "Peace be to you. Do not fear" — divine peace directly displaces terror; (2) Est 9:22 — "sorrow turned into gladness and mourning into a holiday" (in the context of Purim rest/peace); (3) 1Sa 1:17-18 — Hannah went away and "her face was no longer sad" after Eli's peace-blessing; (4) Phili 4:7 — peace guards the heart against anxiety (Phili 4:6 context: "do not be anxious about anything... and the peace of God will guard"). Peace is the affective resolution of anxiety, fear, and sorrow. Its sustained presence does not bypass affect — peace-bearing people still weep, still feel — but it prevents affect from becoming debilitating or destructive. The person in peace can feel sorrow without being overwhelmed by it. |
| OBS-117-T2-068 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Judg 6:23 | The affective engagement reveals that peace is not emotional neutrality or the suppression of feeling but the condition in which affect functions rightly — neither overwhelming the person (anxiety, terror) nor being inaccessible to them (the peaceless Lam 3:17 — "forgotten what happiness is"). Peace is the affective ground: the person who has shalom can feel the full range of affect without being destroyed by negative affect or alienated from positive affect. This is a crucial distinction for the programme: peace is not the absence of feeling but the condition in which feeling is held and expressed rightly. |
| OBS-117-T2-074 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Dan 10:19 | Peace enables agency — the peaceful person is constitutionally equipped to act in the world from a stable inner base rather than from reactive anxiety. Evidence: (1) Dan 10:19 — "peace be with you; be strong and of good courage" — the angelic peace-gift produces strength and courage for action; peace precedes and enables Daniel's capacity to act on the vision; (2) Isa 32:17 — "the effect of righteousness will be peace, and the result of righteousness, quietness and trust forever" — the peace condition produces trust, which is the basis for courageous action; (3) Deu 28:65 reverse — the absence of peace produces the "trembling heart" and "languishing soul" that impair agency; fearful and anxious people cannot act decisively. Conversely: complacent ease (H7600 group 413-001) impairs agency by producing false security and contempt for consequences — a corrupted form of "peace" that disengages agency. |
| OBS-117-T2-075 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Dan 10:19 | The agency pattern reveals that authentic peace is not passive or quietist but enables robust, courageous action in the world. The peaceful person is not inactive — Mordecai seeks welfare, the peacemakers sow righteousness, Christ makes peace through the cross. The silence/stillness vocabulary names the inner orientation that enables agency, not the absence of agency. The contrast with complacent ease (H7600 413-001) is decisive: the person who is "at ease in Zion" (Amo 6:1) is precisely the person who does not act when they should — complacency impairs agency. Authentic shalom liberates agency; false peace suppresses it. |
| OBS-117-T2-103 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Dan 10:19 | Yes — angelic and demonic dimensions are both evidenced: (1) Angelic: Dan 10:19 — the angelic being speaks "peace be with you; be strong and of good courage" — angelic peace-announcement addressing Daniel's inner terror; the messenger mediates divine peace to the human person; Luk 2:14 (not in anchor verses but within G1515 scope — "peace on earth among those with whom he is pleased" — the angelic announcement of peace at Christ's birth); (2) Demonic: Mar 4:39 — "Peace! Be still!" addressed to the wind and sea (G4623, G5392 context — prior session OBS-117-131/132): the elemental forces stilled by Christ's command imply a disordering agency that had disrupted the peace; (3) Rev 8:1 (G4602) — heavenly silence at the seventh seal: the whole heavenly assembly participates in the cosmic peace-threshold. |
| OBS-117-T2-105 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Dan 10:19 | Yes — Dan 10:19 establishes angelic mediation of peace directly: "peace be with you; be strong and of good courage" — the angelic being speaks peace to Daniel as a constitutive part of strengthening him for the vision. The mediation is: divine peace → angelic proclamation → human inner-being reception → strengthening. This establishes angels as genuine mediators of peace in the biblical data, not merely observers. The Christmas announcement (Luk 2:14) follows the same pattern: angelic chorus → peace proclaimed to earth → the incarnate peace-person arrives. The angelic mediation of peace is not merely formal (announcing) but apparently effective (Daniel's fear is addressed and he is strengthened). |
| OBS-117-T2-110 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Judg 6:23 | The data identifies multiple mechanisms: (1) Divine word/proclamation: Judg 6:23 ("Peace be to you") — the spoken word of peace from God or his messenger produces the inner shift from terror to peace; Joh 14:27 ("my peace I give to you") — Christ's word-gift; the proclamation is a mechanism; (2) Conscience-activation: Psa 32:3-5 — the mechanism is confession activating what suppressed conscience had blocked; the act of acknowledgment opens the peace-channel; (3) Cognitive re-direction: Isa 26:3 — the mechanism is the deliberate directing of the mind toward God; (4) Discipline and training: Heb 12:11 — the mechanism is the sustained experience of discipline by a trainer, producing peace as fruit over time; (5) Cross-accomplishment: Col 1:20 — the mechanism is Christ's blood of the cross making peace; a historical accomplished act; (6) Spirit indwelling: Gal 5:22 — the Spirit's presence produces peace as fruit through the mechanism of indwelling and progressive formation. |
| OBS-117-T2-111 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Judg 6:23 | Yes — the mechanisms differ by context: (1) Crisis/encounter context: divine word is the immediate mechanism (Judg 6:23, Dan 10:19, Joh 14:27) — peace comes through an encounter with divine presence or word; (2) Moral failure context: conscience-activation and confession are the mechanism (Psa 32:3-5) — the route back from peacelessness through sin is through honest acknowledgment; (3) Cognitive orientation context: sustained mind-direction is the mechanism (Isa 26:3, Rom 8:6) — for the ongoing inner condition of peace, the mechanism is daily cognitive orientation; (4) Formative context: discipline over time is the mechanism (Heb 12:11) — peace-as-character is formed through sustained training rather than instantaneous receipt; (5) Eschatological/cosmic context: Christ's cross is the mechanism (Col 1:20, Isa 53:5) — for the foundational peace-with-God and cosmic peace, the mechanism is unique historical accomplishment. No single mechanism covers all contexts. |
| OBS-117-T2-148 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Judg 6:23 | Primary contextual settings: (1) Covenantal: the covenant-of-peace texts (Num 6:26, Isa 54:10, Eze 34:25/37:26) — peace is given and confirmed in covenantal ceremony and prophetic announcement; (2) Liturgical/worship: Psa 4:8, 62:5, 85:8, 119:165, 131:2 — the psalmic context is personal worship and prayer; peace is experienced and expressed in the devotional posture; (3) Prophetic warning/lament: Isa 28:12, 30:15, Jer 6:14, Lam 3:17 — the prophetic context of peace refused, false peace proclaimed, and the soul bereft; (4) Eschatological vision: Isa 9:6/7, 32:18, Mic 5:5, Eze 34:25 — messianic and eschatological peace in prophetic vision; (5) Epistolary/communal: Rom 5:1, Phili 4:7, Eph 2:14, 1Th 5:23 — NT peace in the context of the Christian community and Paul's pastoral letters; (6) Crisis/encounter: Judg 6:23, Dan 10:19 — peace given in moments of personal encounter with the divine. The richest contextual setting is prophetic (both warning and vision) — the prophets carry the fullest peace theology. |

**Identity & meaning**

1. Strong's: `H3372H` · Lang: Hebrew · Owner: OWNER
2. Registry: R011 awe · Legacy C-cluster: C03
3. Sub-group: —
4. Term status: extracted · Evidential: — · Occurrences: 111
5. Patch-authoring refs: `mti_id=1682` · `md_version=1` · `vc_status=not_done`

Fellowship can be both initiating event and sustaining condition. |

Fellowship amplifies and conforms character to the fellowship object's nature. |

| OBS-030-T2-145 | OBSERVATION | Jer 44:10 | The presence of contrition reveals an image-bearer in truthful relation to their own creaturely condition — the person whose inner being is permeable to divine assessment. Absence of contrition (the hardened heart of Jer 44:10) reveals an image-bearer closed to this truth — self-sufficient, resistant to divine word. The hardened alternative is therefore an image-deficiency: the person who will not receive the divine verdict about their condition. OBS-030-028, OBS-030-047, OBS-030-062. |
| OBS-030-T2-151 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Jer 44:10 | Contrition is primarily a settled inner-being condition — not an act, not a transient feeling, but a state the person inhabits. The adjectival vocabulary (dak.ka — "the contrite," na.kheh — "the crippled/contrite") designates a person characterised by this condition. However, contrition has a verbal history (the process of being crushed precedes the settled state) and can be refused (Jer 44:10), which means the will is implicated. It is best characterised as: a settled inner condition produced by encounter (with God, with moral reality) that the will can resist but not generate by autonomous decision. OBS-030-009, OBS-030-021, OBS-030-047. |
| OBS-030-T2-154 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Jer 44:10 | The structural opposite is pride — the inner posture of self-elevation that refuses lowliness before God. Isa 57:15 presents the contrast architecturally: the holy God dwells with the lowly and contrite, not with the self-elevated. Jer 44:10 presents the active refusal: "they have not humbled themselves, nor have they feared." The hardened inner being that will not receive the weight of its own moral condition before God is the opposite of contrition. OBS-030-028, OBS-030-034, OBS-030-047. |
| OBS-030-T2-165 | OBSERVATION | Jer 44:10 | Three enabling conditions from Isa 66:2 — humility (lowly posture before God), contrition (crushed spirit — the condition itself names its own ground), and trembling at God's word (orientation toward divine speech). From the broader verse evidence: honest self-knowledge before God (the recognition of having caused actual harm, not surface shame — OBS-030-001); inner permeability rather than hardness (the opposite of Jer 44:10's hardened alternative — OBS-030-028). The enabling condition is fundamentally the absence of self-sufficiency — the openness of the inner being to divine assessment. OBS-030-001, OBS-030-028, OBS-030-060. |
| OBS-030-T2-166 | OBSERVATION | Jer 44:10 | From Jer 44:10: failure to humble oneself, failure to fear God, failure to walk in God's law — these three together describe the hardened alternative. Pride (self-elevation before God) is the structural blocker (Isa 57:15 by contrast). Merit-logic — the claim that ritual performance has covered the moral debt (Psa 51:16) — also blocks genuine contrition by providing an alternative to inner brokenness. OBS-030-028, OBS-030-047, OBS-030-053. |
| OBS-030-T2-167 | OBSERVATION | Jer 44:10 | Jer 44:10 provides the clearest evidence: the un-contrite person is characterised by hardness (not humbled), absence of fear (not trembling), and orientation away from God's word (not walking in the law). The inner-being state is one of self-enclosure — the inner being turned back on itself, impermeable to divine assessment. The refusal of contrition is not passive neutrality but active self-protection of the inner being from the weight of its own moral condition. *New finding: the person who refuses contrition is characterised by inner self-enclosure — an active impermeability rather than a neutral absence of feeling.* OBS-030-028, OBS-030-047. |
| OBS-030-T2-190 | OBSERVATION | Jer 44:10 | Contrition originates in the encounter between divine holiness and human moral condition — it is produced by relational encounter, not generated from within by autonomous human decision. The origin is constitutionally external to the self (divine holiness as the generative cause) but experienced internally (at the spirit and heart level). The passive grammar of the vocabulary (being crushed, being smitten) confirms the external origin. However, the will is implicated in whether the person remains open or hardens (Jer 44:10 — the refusal of contrition). OBS-030-007, OBS-030-045, OBS-030-047. |
| OBS-030-T2-196 | OBSERVATION | Jer 44:10 | Contrition deepens perceptive capacity in one specific direction: it opens the person to receive divine address (trembling at God's word — Isa 66:2). The contrite person is not closed to divine communication but particularly open to it. The hardened alternative (Jer 44:10 — not walking in God's law) implies perceptive closure to divine word. *New finding: contrition deepens the perceptive capacity for divine address — the contrite person is specifically receptive to God's word in a way the hardened person is not.* OBS-030-060, OBS-030-028. |
| OBS-030-T2-197 | OBSERVATION | Jer 44:10 | The pattern reveals contrition as a perceptive-opening event — the inner breaking simultaneously opens the person to divine address. The hardened heart is perceptively closed; the contrite heart is perceptively receptive. Contrition is the condition in which the perceptive faculty is most available to God's word and God's presence. OBS-030-028, OBS-030-060, OBS-030-062. |
| OBS-030-T2-199 | OBSERVATION | Jer 44:10 | Contrition deepens self-cognition — it requires and produces honest self-knowledge. The hardened alternative (Jer 44:10) is cognitively closed — the un-contrite person does not receive the divine word because cognitive closure prevents it. OBS-030-001, OBS-030-028, OBS-030-047. |
| OBS-030-T2-207 | OBSERVATION | Jer 44:10 | Yes — the will is implicated in whether contrition is received or refused. Isa 66:2 identifies the contrite person as one who trembles at God's word — an orientation that involves volitional submission to divine address. However, the origin of contrition is not primarily a volitional act — the person does not choose to be crushed. The will is present in the receiving or refusing, not in the generating. | OBS-062-T2-201 | OBSERVATION | Psa 119:63 | Fellowship originates from two sources depending on mode: (1) Divine initiative — God joins (Eze 37:19), God promises (2Pe 1:4), the Spirit mediates (2Cor 13:14). (2) Human volitional alignment — the person joins themselves to (Hithpael reflexive), declares companionship (Psa 119:63), pursues (Phili 3:10). Existential fellowship (Ecc 9:4) is a given of existence — neither divine special initiative nor human choice but the created condition. OBS-062-037, OBS-062-051, OBS-062-045. |

| OBS-062-T2-218 | OBSERVATION | Psa 119:63 | Yes — volition is central. The companionship mode (Psa 119:63 — "I am a companion") is a volitional declaration. The pursuit mode (Phili 3:10 — "that I may know him") is aspirational volition. The Hithpael stem of H2266 (join oneself to — reflexive volitional) is the grammatical form of volitional self-joining. OBS-062-048, OBS-062-055, OBS-062-007. |
| OBS-062-T2-219 | OBSERVATION | Psa 119:63 | Fellowship directs and eventually fixes volition. Initial volitional alignment toward an object (Psa 119:63 declared companionship; Phili 3:10 aspirational pursuit) produces habitual alignment that over time becomes constitutional (Jer 13:23 — fixed character). The volitional act of self-joining (Hithpael) is the beginning; constitutional fixing is the endpoint. OBS-062-048, OBS-062-052, OBS-062-055. |
| OBS-062-T2-221 | OBSERVATION | Psa 119:63 | Yes — fellowship involves agency in the self-joining modes. The Hithpael stem (reflexive — "I join myself to") is an agentive act. Paul's pursuit of fellowship (Phili 3:10) is an agentive pursuit. Declaratory companionship (Psa 119:63) is an agentive declaration. OBS-062-048, OBS-062-055, OBS-062-007. |
| OBS-062-T2-224 | OBSERVATION | Psa 119:63 | Yes — deeply. Fellowship with God-fearers produces righteous character (Psa 119:63); fellowship with thieves produces corrupt character (Isa 1:23). Moral complicity (Mat 23:30) is explicitly a moral-evaluative fellowship act. 2Cor 6:14 poses the incompatibility of light-and-darkness fellowship as a moral-evaluative question. OBS-062-048, OBS-062-049, OBS-062-057, OBS-062-059. |
| OBS-062-T2-230 | OBSERVATION | Psa 119:63 | Yes — Psa 119:63 ("I am a companion of all who fear you, of those who keep your precepts") is the paradigm conscientiousness statement within fellowship: an integrated moral alignment (those who fear God and keep his precepts) expressed as a stable relational posture. OBS-062-048. |
| OBS-062-T2-239 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Psa 119:63 | Yes — and this is the most richly evidenced relational direction in the registry. Psa 119:63 (declaring companionship with God-fearers as orientation toward God), Phili 3:10 (pursuing fellowship of Christ's sufferings), 1Jo 1:3 (fellowship with Father and Son), 2Pe 1:4 (escaping corruption to participate in divine nature). OBS-062-048, OBS-062-055, OBS-062-056, OBS-062-058. |
| OBS-062-T2-242 | OBSERVATION | Psa 119:63 | Yes — richly evidenced. Ecc 4:10 (the friend who lifts when one falls), Psa 119:63 (companion of God-fearers as community formation), Mal 2:14 (covenant companion), Isa 1:23 (companion of thieves as moral-formation warning), 2Cor 1:7 (sharing comfort proportionate to sharing suffering). OBS-062-050, OBS-062-054, OBS-062-057, OBS-062-031. |
| OBS-062-T2-256 | VERSE_PATTERN | Psa 119:63 | Yes — a formation sequence: (1) Volitional alignment / self-joining (Psa 119:63, Phili 3:10 — initiating acts); (2) Habitual participation (sustained fellowship over time); (3) Constitutional formation (Jer 13:23 — fixed character as the endpoint). For divine nature participation (2Pe 1:4): (1) Receipt of divine promise; (2) Escape from corrupting desire; (3) Participation in divine nature. OBS-062-048, OBS-062-052, OBS-062-058. |
| OBS-062-T2-262 | OBSERVATION | Psa 119:63 | Yes — habitual fellowship is the primary mechanism of character formation in this registry. The companionship-habituation arc (Psa 119:63 → Jer 13:23) is a sanctification arc: sustained alignment with God-fearers forms righteous character. 2Pe 1:4's divine nature participation is the telos of the fellowship-sanctification arc. OBS-062-048, OBS-062-052, OBS-062-058. |
| OBS-064-T2-141 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Psa 130:4 | The verse evidence reveals God as the one who possesses and initiates forgiveness — the divine character is explicitly named as the origin-point of the act. Psa 130:4 ("there is forgiveness with you") locates forgiveness in the divine person as a possession. Psa 86:5 names God as "good and forgiving (*sal.lach*), abounding in steadfast love" — placing forgiveness-readiness as a divine character attribute co-equal with goodness and steadfast love. Dan 9:9 — "to the Lord our God belong mercy and forgiveness." The characteristic reflected is God's willingness to release legitimate claims on behalf of the offender — the divine character of not exacting the full measure of justice when relationship is possible. OBS-064-003, OBS-064-019, OBS-064-020. |
| OBS-064-T2-147 | OBSERVATION | Psa 130:4 | Both shared and asymmetric. Shared: the same act-structure (releasing a claim) is present in both divine and human forgiveness; both use aphiēmi in the NT. Asymmetric: God forgives from a position of absolute righteous authority; the human forgives from a position of received forgiveness — human forgiveness is structurally derivative of the divine. The sharing is real but the basis differs. OBS-064-006. |
| OBS-064-T2-151 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Psa 130:4 | "Forgiveness" signals the release of a legitimate claim — not the denial that the claim existed but the cancellation of it. The Hebrew salach names a divine-exclusive releasing act. The Greek aphiēmi names a releasing/sending-away. The name signals: (1) an act (not a feeling); (2) releasing (not denying or minimising); (3) a claim that was legitimate (the offence was real). The programme name "forgiveness" therefore carries three implicit signals: something real was owed, the creditor releases the debtor, the debt is cancelled not transferred. OBS-064-003, OBS-064-004, OBS-064-005. |
| OBS-064-T2-152 | ETYMOLOGY | Psa 130:4 | H5545 (sa.lach — verb): to forgive; exclusively divine subject in OT. H5546 (sal.lach — adjective): forgiving as dispositional character attribute of God (Psa 86:5 alone). H5547 (se.li.chah — noun): forgiveness as abstract quality possessed by God (Psa 130:4, Dan 9:9, Neh 9:17). The three Hebrew forms name the same reality from three angles: act (verb), disposition (adjective), possession (noun). At the definitional level the Hebrew roots reveal that forgiveness is: exclusively divine at its source, characterological in God's being (it describes who God is, not just what God does), and a possession that God has and can extend. OBS-064-003, OBS-064-019, OBS-064-020. |
| OBS-064-T2-153 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Psa 130:4 | Directional: forgiveness moves from God toward the offender (Psa 130:4 — forgiveness is "with" God and moves toward the one who calls); from the offended toward the offender (horizontal mode). Relational: forgiveness is constitutively relational — it requires at minimum two parties and a prior breach. Constitutional: forgiveness received constitutes the person differently — it produces love (Luk 7:47) and reverential fear (Psa 130:4), reshaping the inner-being orientation of the recipient. OBS-064-018, OBS-064-019, OBS-064-029. |
| OBS-064-T2-156 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Psa 130:4 | Forgiveness is the relational act of releasing a legitimate claim against an offender — the cancellation of a debt rather than its denial. It operates in four modes (covenantal-objective, divine relational-personal, human horizontal, intercessory), each sharing the single act-structure of releasing-a-hold. It is grounded in divine character (the offended party's disposition, not the offender's merit), produces two specific downstream inner states (love, reverence), and creates the relational condition for restored access. OBS-064-003, OBS-064-018, OBS-064-029. |
| OBS-064-T2-163 | VERSE_PATTERN | Psa 130:4 | Two specific immediate inner states are named: (1) Love — Luk 7:47 establishes a quantity-proportional causal chain: "she loved much because she was forgiven much; he who is forgiven little loves little." Love is the immediate inner-being response to received forgiveness. (2) Reverential fear/awe — Psa 130:4 ("there is forgiveness with you, that you may be feared"). Encountering forgiveness as a divine quality produces reverence rather than presumption. OBS-064-020, OBS-064-021, OBS-064-029. |
| OBS-064-T2-164 | VERSE_PATTERN | Psa 130:4 | The immediate response varies by mode and direction. Receiving forgiveness personally: love (Luk 7:47), relief of guilt-burden (implied by the "you are forgiven" pronouncement pattern). Encountering forgiveness as divine quality: reverential fear (Psa 130:4). Extending forgiveness: inner release of the claim in the withholder (implied by Mat 18:35 — heart-level release as the act itself). Withholding forgiveness: inner-life poison/torment (Mat 18:34, OBS-064-001). OBS-064-029, OBS-064-021. |
| OBS-064-T2-172 | OBSERVATION | Psa 130:4 | Relational Disposition is supported by the dominant subject pattern: God as the one who forgives (divine Relational Disposition toward the human), and the human as commanded to forgive (horizontal Relational Disposition). The act-structure (releasing-a-claim) is inherently relational — it requires a relationship within which the claim exists. OBS-064-007, OBS-064-010. |
| OBS-064-T2-192 | OBSERVATION | Psa 130:4 | Forgiveness originates in divine character — specifically the divine readiness/disposition (sal.lach — Psa 86:5) and the divine possession of forgiveness (se.li.chah — Psa 130:4, Dan 9:9). The constitutional origin of forgiveness is entirely from God in its vertical form; in the horizontal human form, it is derived from having received the vertical. OBS-064-003, OBS-064-019, OBS-064-020. |
| OBS-064-T2-197 | OBSERVATION | Psa 130:4 | Yes — perception is engaged in both the giving and receiving directions. In the giving direction: the offended person must perceive the magnitude of the offence to be released — the correct perception of what is owed is the prerequisite for knowing what is being released. In the receiving direction: Psa 130:4 establishes that encountering divine forgiveness as a quality produces reverential awe — a perceptive-affective response to what is perceived about God. OBS-064-020, OBS-064-021. |
| OBS-064-T2-198 | OBSERVATION | Psa 130:4 | Forgiveness deepens and opens perception — specifically perception of divine character. Psa 130:4 (forgiveness encountered → reverential fear produced) implies that the encounter with forgiveness as a divine quality sharpens perception of who God is. The Pharisee's limited love (Luk 7:47 — "forgiven little, loves little") implies limited perception of the magnitude of the forgiveness — perception of the gift's magnitude determines the love-response. OBS-064-020, OBS-064-029. |
| OBS-064-T2-205 | OBSERVATION | Psa 130:4 | Yes — deeply. Love (agapē) is the named downstream affective state produced by forgiveness received (Luk 7:47). Reverential fear (awe) is produced by encountering forgiveness as a divine quality (Psa 130:4). The visceral compassion (splagchnizomai — Mat 18:27) is the named affective precondition for extending forgiveness. Forgiveness therefore engages affect at both ends: as a prerequisite (compassion producing the act) and as an outcome (love and reverence produced by receiving the act). OBS-064-020, OBS-064-021, OBS-064-022, OBS-064-029. |
| OBS-064-T2-206 | OBSERVATION | Psa 130:4 | Forgiveness deepens affect in the receiving direction (love produced, Luk 7:47 — proportional to the depth of the forgiveness received) and deepens reverential fear (Psa 130:4). In the giving direction, forgiveness requires and expresses somatic compassion. Withholding forgiveness degrades affect — the torment-state of Mat 18:34 is an affective state of inner imprisonment. OBS-064-029, OBS-064-032. |
| OBS-064-T2-214 | OBSERVATION | Psa 130:4 | Yes — moral evaluation is intrinsic to forgiveness. The act of forgiving requires accurate assessment of the moral offence (what is being released) and the moral standing of the parties (the offended has a legitimate claim; the offender is genuinely guilty). Psa 130:4's reverential-fear response to encountering divine forgiveness involves the moral evaluative recognition that God does not owe forgiveness but gives it. OBS-064-020, OBS-064-021. |
| OBS-064-T2-229 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Psa 130:4 | Yes — the seeking-forgiveness direction (human seeking divine forgiveness) is richly evidenced: Dan 9:19 (Daniel's intercession), Psa 130:4 (waiting for the Lord with hope for forgiveness), 1Jo 1:9 (confession → forgiveness), Act 2:38 (repentance for forgiveness). OBS-064-015, OBS-064-020, OBS-064-022. |
| OBS-064-T2-230 | OBSERVATION | Psa 130:4 | The inner posture required for the human-to-God direction: dependence (Dan 9:9 — grounding the plea in God's character, not human merit), honest self-assessment (1Jo 1:9 — confession names the condition accurately), and hope in divine forgiveness-character (Psa 130:4 — waiting for the Lord because forgiveness is with him). The posture is constitutively non-merit-claiming. OBS-064-016, OBS-064-022. |
| OBS-064-T2-244 | OBSERVATION | Psa 130:4 | Both. Condition: forgiveness received transforms the person's standing before God (from guilt-bearing to guilt-free — the forensic condition changes). Orientation: the sustained receipt of forgiveness produces love-orientation (Luk 7:47) and reverential fear (Psa 130:4) as stable inner dispositions. OBS-064-029, OBS-064-020. |
| OBS-064-T2-274 | ETYMOLOGY | Psa 130:4 | H5545 (sa.lach — verb): to forgive; exclusive divine subject. H5546 (sal.lach — adjective): forgiving as divine character; Psa 86:5 sole occurrence. H5547 (se.li.chah — noun): forgiveness as divine possession; Psa 130:4, Dan 9:9, Neh 9:17. G0859 (afesis — noun): forgiveness as state/condition; predominantly in "forgiveness of sins" phrase. G0863G/H/I: three sub-entries of aphiēmi ("to release: leave"; "to release: forgive"; "to release: permit"). Root meaning H5545: uncertain etymology — a technical term for divine forgiveness with no clear concrete root image. Root meaning G0863: apo (away from) + hiēmi (to send/let go) = to send away, release a hold. OBS-064-003, OBS-064-004, OBS-064-005. |
| OBS-064-T2-283 | VERSE_ANNOTATION | Psa 130:4 | Psa 130:4 — H5547 (se.li.chah noun) functions as the ground of hope: "there is forgiveness with you, that you may be feared." The noun functions as the asserted divine quality on which the psalmist's hope rests. The function is declaratory-of-divine-character rather than describing an act already performed or requesting one. OBS-064-020. |
| OBS-060-T2-031 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Mal 2:5 | The primary dimension is Moral Character — specifically as the enacted expression of covenantal commitment. This is supported by the largest group (872-001, 37 relevant verses, KEYWORD_STRONG confidence) whose description names "divine giving as the expression of covenant faithfulness — God's giving of land, promise, and blessing as the embodiment of his inner covenantal commitment." The registry-level dimension assignment 'Moral/Conscience' is consistent with this. The covenantal dimension of na.tan (commitment enacted over generations, across changing circumstances, regardless of human merit) most directly expresses Moral Character as a dimension — the giving is the character made visible. This determination addresses DIM-60-001 (OBS-060-053): the primary dimension of the registry is Moral Character, but the registry carries four additional significant dimensions (Relational Disposition, Cognition, Transformation, DHC) that the single registry-level assignment does not capture. |
| OBS-060-T2-032 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Mal 2:5 | The Moral Character classification is supported by: (a) Group 872-001 (37 verses, KEYWORD_STRONG) — the covenant-faithfulness giving texts centre on God's character expressed in enacted commitment over time: Gen 12:7, Gen 15:18, Neh 9:8 ("You found his heart faithful before you, and made with him the covenant to give..."), Mal 2:5 ("My covenant with him was one of life and peace, and I gave them to him"). | OBS-060-T2-064 | OBSERVATION | Neh 9:32 | The characteristic deepens memory in its covenantal mode: the accumulated record of divine giving across generations forms the memory-structure of Israel's inner-being identity. Each new giving adds to the memory of prior giving, deepening the narrative foundation of trust. Neh 9 (the long Levitical prayer) is itself a memory-act: reciting the history of divine giving as the basis of present covenantal renewal. Hos 2:15 invokes Exodus memory as the ground of eschatological hope — the memory of what God gave before shapes the expectation of what he will give again. The characteristic does not impair memory in any evidenced instance; it is constitutively tied to the faithfulness of remembered giving. |

<a id="t-G5399"></a>
### G5399 fobeō — to fear (`mti_id=292`)

**Identity & meaning**

1. Strong's: `G5399` · Lang: Greek · Owner: OWNER
2. Registry: R061 fear · Legacy C-cluster: C06
3. Sub-group: —
4. Term status: extracted · Evidential: — · Occurrences: 441
5. Patch-authoring refs: `mti_id=292` · `md_version=1` · `vc_status=not_done`
6. Mounce short-def: to fear, be afraid, alarmed, in some contexts improper and an impediment to faith and love; to reverence, respect, worship, in other contexts a proper fear for God, a deep reverence and awe

**Verses:** 83 distinct locations (see §2 for the verse table grouped by sub-group).

**Group memberships (3)**

| Group ID | Code | Description | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| 921 | 292-001 | Term names the theophanic or miraculous inner fear — the overwhelming inner response to divine presence, miracle, or power, leading to awe and worship |  |
| 922 | 292-002 | Term names the reverential fear of God as the inner orientation of godly life — fearing God who judges both body and soul; the inner disposition that shapes worship and ethics |  |
| 923 | 292-003 | Term names the practical or self-interested inner fear before humans or consequences — the inner calculation of social, political, or physical danger that drives action |  |

**Findings — direct (Strong's mention) (1)**

| Finding ID | Type | Anchor verses | Excerpt |
|---|---|---|---|
| DIM-61-001 | DIMENSION_REVIEW |  | fobeō (G5399) shows a tripartite inner-being structure: (1) theophanic/miraculous fear leading to worship (Spiritual/God-ward), (2) reverential life-shaping fear of God (Spiritual/God-ward), (3) practical self-interested fear before humans or consequences (Affective/Emotional). This tripartite structure is the most analytically important pattern in Registry 61 and should be the organising frame for Session B analysis. |

OBS-111-031, OBS-111-038, OBS-111-068. |

### H3373 ya.re — afraid (`mti_id=1681`)

**Identity & meaning**

1. Strong's: `H3373` · Lang: Hebrew · Owner: OWNER
2. Registry: R011 awe · Legacy C-cluster: C03
3. Sub-group: —
4. Term status: extracted · Evidential: — · Occurrences: 65
5. Patch-authoring refs: `mti_id=1681` · `md_version=1` · `vc_status=not_done`

**Verses:** 64 distinct locations (see §2 for the verse table grouped by sub-group).

**Group memberships (2)**

| Group ID | Code | Description | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| 257 | 1681-001 | God-fearer as inner-being identity — those characterised by reverence for God as their defining mark, recipients of divine attention and blessing |  |
| 258 | 1681-002 | Fear as inner state of anxiety or dread directed at human threats — inner person unsettled by danger, opposition, or uncertain outcomes |  |

**Findings — direct (Strong's mention) (0)**

(none)

**Findings — via anchor verse (3 unique)**

| Finding ID | Type | Matched anchor refs | Excerpt |
|---|---|---|---|
| OBS-034-T2-056 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Psa 25:14 | Yes — hearing is the perceptive faculty most centrally engaged. Exo 19:5: "if you will indeed obey my voice and keep my covenant" — covenantal reception requires hearing God's voice (OBS-034-030; R213 listen, 13 shared verses). Jer 11:8: "they did not obey or incline their ear" — covenant breach is framed as a failure of inner hearing. Heb 8:9: "they did not continue in my covenant" follows from "I took them by the hand to bring them out of Egypt" — the context of covenant departure is failure to attend. Deu 7:9: "those who love him and keep his commandments" — commanded hearing and keeping go together. The inner ear — the faculty of attentive receptive listening — is structurally connected to covenant-keeping. Spiritual discernment also appears: Psa 25:14: "the friendship of the Lord is for those who fear him, and he makes known to them his covenant" — discernment of God's covenant is given to those who fear him. The perceptive faculty operates as the gateway to covenant engagement. |
| OBS-034-T2-057 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Psa 25:14 | Covenant engagement enables and deepens perception; covenant breach impairs it. For enabling: Psa 25:14 — God makes known his covenant to those who fear him; the covenant-keeping person receives deeper discernment of God's reality and purposes. The new covenant explicitly promises restored perception: "they shall all know me" (Jer 31:34) — the new covenant produces a knowing that is itself a form of deep inner perception of God. For impairing: 2 Cor 3:14 — "their minds were hardened... a veil remains" (OBS-034-072). The old covenant read without Christ impairs cognitive-perceptive engagement; the veil blocks what was meant to be seen and known. Covenant-breaking also impairs — Jer 11:8 frames covenant breach as failure to incline the ear: the breaking of the covenantal relationship is accompanied by a closing of the perceptive faculty. |
| OBS-034-T2-058 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Psa 25:14 | The pattern reveals that covenant is not a self-activating inner-being reality — it depends on an open perceptive faculty as its gateway. Covenant cannot be received by the person who will not hear; it cannot transform the person whose perceptive faculty is veiled or hardened. Conversely, the new covenant's promise is precisely to restore and enable perception: writing on the heart produces knowing (Jer 31:34), and knowing is a form of heightened inner perception of God. This means covenant and perception have a reciprocal relationship: open perception enables covenant reception; covenant transformation deepens and enlarges perception. The pattern shows that covenant is the structured framework within which the inner perceptive faculty either opens toward God (covenant faithfulness) or closes away from him (covenant breach and hardening). |

|---|---|---|---|
| DIM-11-001 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | Psa 111:10 | Awe spans both Affective/Emotional and Spiritual/God-ward dimensions. God-ward groups (1682-001, 1682-003, 703-002, 703-003) show that the deepest fear/awe content is Spiritual/God-ward rather than merely affective. Session B should examine whether awe functions as a distinct inner-being category integrating affective intensity and God-ward orientation — the two are inseparable in the data. |
| OBS-067-T2-028 | VERSE_PATTERN | Pro 15:16 | Three enabling inner conditions converge (SBF-067-Q014): (1) Proximity/orientation toward God — Psa 73:28 ("it is good to be near God"). The inner condition of nearness, of having God as one's refuge, enables reception of what is genuinely good. (2) Fear of the Lord — Pro 15:16 ("better is a little with the fear of the Lord"). The inner posture of reverential dependence is the ground of receiving the good. (3) Spirit-filling — Gal 5:22 / Rom 15:14. The Spirit's presence in the inner being produces goodness and enables its reception and expression. These three are not independent conditions — they converge on a single posture: the person oriented toward God, filled by his Spirit, whose inner life has been reoriented toward the source of goodness. Additionally, trust/faith is named as the condition for ongoing experience of divine chrēstotēs (Rom 11:22 — "provided you continue in his kindness"). (OBS-067-OBS-025, OBS-067-OBS-029, SBF-067-Q014) |
| OBS-067-T2-033 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Pro 15:16 | Secondary dimensions confirmed: Cognition (03) — 884-004 (comparative wisdom evaluation) and 884-006 (moral verdict assessment) both require the cognitive evaluation faculty. Volition (04) — 884-008 (volitional preference idiom, 40 verses) and 885-001 (Spirit-produced goodness as resolve, 2Th 1:11). The secondary dimensions do not compete with the primary — they represent the multi-modal nature of the characteristic. Moral Character is primary because it characterises the person's inner being as good; Cognition is secondary because the moral evaluation faculty is engaged in assessing what is good; Volition is secondary because goodness both criteria the will and reconstitutes it. The WARN item #3 (no dim_review record) is noted: these assignments are based on Stage 2a observation and are analytically grounded but have not passed a formal dimension review process. (OBS-067-OBS-011, OBS-067-OBS-012, OBS-067-OBS-014, OBS-067-OBS-016) |
| OBS-067-T2-041 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Pro 15:16 | Direct mind-location is not explicitly named in the verse evidence. However, the cognitive register of goodness is evidenced through the dimension assignment: 884-004 (comparative wisdom evaluation) and 884-006 (moral verdict) are assigned Cognition (03), indicating that the mind's evaluative and discerning function is engaged. The comparative wisdom idiom ("better than") is a cognitive-evaluative operation — assessing and ranking goods. This is a mind-faculty operation even if the term "mind" is not explicitly used. Rom 15:14 pairs goodness with "all knowledge" in the same clause — "full of goodness, filled with all knowledge" — suggesting that goodness and cognitive knowledge are related inner-being qualities. The evidence locates goodness at the evaluative level of mind-function, but explicit mind-language is absent. (OBS-067-OBS-012, OBS-067-OBS-025) |
| OBS-067-T2-042 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Pro 15:16 | The evaluative and discerning aspect of the mind is what goodness engages. The comparative wisdom mode (884-004) engages the mind's capacity to rank and assess — distinguishing greater goods from lesser goods. The moral verdict mode (884-006) engages the mind's capacity to assess conduct against a standard. The volitional-preference mode (884-008) engages the mind's evaluative role in choice — "what seems good to you" implies an assessment before a decision. This is the mind functioning as moral evaluator — not primarily as rational analyst but as the faculty of moral discernment. The fact that Cognition is a secondary dimension for this characteristic (Q&A-036) confirms the engagement but at a secondary level. (OBS-067-OBS-012, OBS-067-OBS-014, SBF-067-Q088) |
| OBS-067-T2-056 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Pro 15:16 | Yes — cognition is a secondary dimension of goodness (confirmed at Q&A-036). The cognitive engagement takes three forms: (1) Evaluative cognition — the comparative wisdom mode (884-004) requires ranking and assessing goods against each other. "Better than" implies a knowing that orders and ranks. (2) Moral assessment cognition — the not-good verdict mode (884-006) requires applying the standard of the good to conduct and naming the verdict. This is a moral-cognitive act. (3) Receptive cognition — Jos 23:14 ("you know in your hearts and souls") names the reception of covenantal knowing as a cognitive act located in the inner being. The mind knows and holds God's good word as an inner-being cognitive reality. (OBS-067-OBS-012, OBS-067-OBS-033, OBS-067-OBS-034) |
| OBS-067-T2-057 | VERSE_PATTERN | Pro 15:16 | Goodness enables and deepens cognition. The comparative wisdom mode actively trains the evaluative intellect — the better-than sayings of 884-004 require and cultivate discerning moral cognition. Rom 15:14 pairs goodness with knowledge in a single characterological portrait: "full of goodness, filled with all knowledge" — suggesting a natural coherence between goodness and cognitive fullness. The absence of goodness impairs cognition: the moral inversion of Mal 2:17 / Jer 44:17 (calling evil good) is a cognitive failure — the evaluative faculty is corrupted. The direction is clear: goodness present deepens moral cognition; goodness absent or distorted impairs it. (OBS-067-OBS-012, OBS-067-OBS-021, OBS-067-OBS-025) |
| OBS-067-T2-058 | VERSE_PATTERN | Pro 15:16 | The cognitive engagement reveals that goodness is not ethically naive or merely affective — it requires intellectual content. The wisdom literature's comparative evaluations demand a capacity for moral reasoning. The pairing of goodness with knowledge (Rom 15:14) suggests that genuine goodness has a cognitive substrate — the person who is good knows what is good and why. This is consistent with the Mic 6:8 revelatory frame ("He has told you what is good") — goodness is disclosed knowledge, not merely felt impulse. The pattern further reveals that goodness in its distorted form (calling evil good) specifically corrupts the cognitive faculty — which implies that genuine goodness and genuine cognition are structurally coherent. (OBS-067-OBS-012, OBS-067-OBS-027, OBS-067-OBS-025) |
| OBS-067-T2-072 | VERSE_PATTERN | Pro 15:16 | Goodness enables and deepens moral evaluation when genuine; distorted goodness specifically impairs it. The enabling function: the standard of the good, as revealed and received (Mic 6:8 — "He has told you what is good"), calibrates the moral evaluation faculty. The person who possesses genuine goodness can accurately assess what is and is not good. The deepening function: the comparative wisdom mode actively trains the evaluative capacity — the better-than sayings develop discernment. The impairing function: Mal 2:17 / Jer 44:17 describe the condition where moral evaluation is inverted — the faculty is functioning but its standard has been corrupted. This is the most severe impairment: the evaluative faculty applied to a false standard produces confident but wrong moral verdicts. (OBS-067-OBS-012, OBS-067-OBS-021, SBF-067-Q065) |
| OBS-067-T2-140 | VERSE_ANNOTATION | Pro 15:16 | The anchor verse corpus spans multiple literary forms, each with distinct interpretive requirements: (1) Prophetic address (Mic 6:8; Eze 36:31): legal covenant-speech, including divine accusation and requirement. Mic 6:8 functions as the verdict of a covenant lawsuit (rib) — God's requirement is stated as the standard against which Israel's failure is measured. Requires: attention to covenantal frame; the "requirement" is not a new imposition but a restoration of what was always known. (2) Wisdom sayings (Pro 15:16; 16:32): comparative instruction for individual moral formation. Requires: attention to the rhetorical purpose of persuasion toward wise living; the better-than structure is pedagogical. (3) Psalms of lament and praise (Psa 34:8; 73:28; 34:8 — crisis context; Psa 119:68 — torah psalm): personal address and corporate declaration. Requires: attention to the experiential context from which the declaration arises. (4) NT epistolary (Rom 2:4; 11:22; Gal 5:22; Col 3:12): doctrinal instruction and paraenesis. Requires: attention to the theological argument in which the verse is embedded. (OBS-067-OBS-027, OBS-067-OBS-042, SBF-067-Q042) |
| OBS-067-T2-142 | VERSE_ANNOTATION | Pro 15:16 | The anchor verse corpus spans a notably broad contextual range: (1) Covenantal-judicial setting (Mic 6:8 — covenant lawsuit; Jos 23:14 — covenant farewell address): the primary human moral goodness verse is set in a judicial-covenantal frame — goodness is the standard of covenant obligation. (2) Liturgical-doxological setting (Psa 34:8; 119:68; doxological refrain): corporate worship and individual prayer as the context for declaring and encountering divine goodness. (3) Wisdom-instructional setting (Pro 15:16; 16:32): educational and formational context for human moral development. (4) Prophetic-restorative setting (Eze 36:31): post-exilic restoration context where goodness is encountered through recognition of its absence. (5) Pauline-pneumatological setting (Gal 5:22; Col 3:12): community formation in the new covenant context. The breadth of contextual settings confirms that goodness is not restricted to a single register of life — it operates across judicial, liturgical, instructional, prophetic, and community contexts. (OBS-067-OBS-027, OBS-067-OBS-042, SBF-067-Q042) |

| OBS-117-T2-066 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Jer 30:10 | Yes — extensively. Peace is itself primarily an experiential/affective condition in many of its manifestations. | OBS-060-T2-031 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Mal 2:5 | The primary dimension is Moral Character — specifically as the enacted expression of covenantal commitment. This is supported by the largest group (872-001, 37 relevant verses, KEYWORD_STRONG confidence) whose description names "divine giving as the expression of covenant faithfulness — God's giving of land, promise, and blessing as the embodiment of his inner covenantal commitment." The registry-level dimension assignment 'Moral/Conscience' is consistent with this. The covenantal dimension of na.tan (commitment enacted over generations, across changing circumstances, regardless of human merit) most directly expresses Moral Character as a dimension — the giving is the character made visible. This determination addresses DIM-60-001 (OBS-060-053): the primary dimension of the registry is Moral Character, but the registry carries four additional significant dimensions (Relational Disposition, Cognition, Transformation, DHC) that the single registry-level assignment does not capture. |
| OBS-060-T2-032 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Mal 2:5 | The Moral Character classification is supported by: (a) Group 872-001 (37 verses, KEYWORD_STRONG) — the covenant-faithfulness giving texts centre on God's character expressed in enacted commitment over time: Gen 12:7, Gen 15:18, Neh 9:8 ("You found his heart faithful before you, and made with him the covenant to give..."), Mal 2:5 ("My covenant with him was one of life and peace, and I gave them to him"). The giving is framed as the expression of God's inner character, not merely a transactional provision. (b) Group 872-004 (11 verses) — the judicial giving-over is also classified as Moral Character, evidencing that God's moral character is expressed in both directions of giving. (c) DIM-60-001 (OBS-060-032, OBS-060-053): the existing finding names the theological/divine-human register of the registry, consistent with Moral Character as the primary dimension for a registry dominated by divine inner-being expression. |

Fear is not love's replacement but its companion. The person who loves God is also the person who properly fears God. |
| OBS-103-T2-115 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Hos 3:5 | The data contains supplication-for-love contexts but not a dedicated seeking term. Lam 3:22 (OBS-103-088): the community crying out for chesed in the midst of desolation is implicit supplication. The Psalms' consistent 'according to your chesed' (Psa 63:3, Psa 78:38) pattern is love-seeking as petition. Hos 3:5 (OBS-103-082): 'they shall come in fear to the Lord and to his goodness' — movement toward God's love/goodness as a seeking-act. However, a specific lexical term for 'seeking love' is not identified in the current data package. Gap: the seeking-term for love may exist in the broader corpus (the Psalms' petition-for-chesed formulae) but is not captured as a named group or anchor in R103's current structure. |
