<a id="t-H2730"></a>
### H2730 cha.red — trembling (`mti_id=310`)

**Identity & meaning**

1. Strong's: `H2730` · Lang: Hebrew · Owner: OWNER
2. Registry: R061 fear · Legacy C-cluster: C06
3. Sub-group: —
4. Term status: extracted · Evidential: — · Occurrences: 6
5. Patch-authoring refs: `mti_id=310` · `md_version=1` · `vc_status=not_done`

**Verses:** 6 distinct locations (see §2 for the verse table grouped by sub-group).

**Group memberships (2)**

| Group ID | Code | Description | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| 940 | 310-001 | Term names the inner condition of trembling at the word of God — the responsive, reverent trembling that characterises the person God looks upon with favour |  |
| 941 | 310-002 | Term names the inner condition of fearful trembling before threatening circumstances or the sacred — the inner agitation of fear or reverent anxiety |  |

**Findings — direct (Strong's mention) (0)**

(none)

**Findings — via anchor verse (45 unique)**

| Finding ID | Type | Matched anchor refs | Excerpt |
|---|---|---|---|
| OBS-030-T2-138 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Isa 66:2 | The verse evidence reveals God as the holy One who dwells with the crushed. Isa 57:15 names God as "the high and lofty One who inhabits eternity, whose name is Holy" and then declares his dwelling with the contrite and lowly spirit. This is not God's mercy or grace in the abstract — it is specifically the divine character of holiness generating a preferential dwelling with the crushed. Isa 66:2 confirms the pattern: "this is the one to whom I will look — he who is humble and contrite in spirit." God's character as holy-and-attentive-to-the-crushed is what contrition reflects or images in the human person. OBS-030-045, OBS-030-062. |
| OBS-030-T2-139 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Isa 66:2 | Scripture is silent about God possessing contrition — explicitly so. The verse evidence consistently frames contrition as the human posture before God, and God as the one who responds to it (draws near, revives, saves). The holiness of God is precisely what produces contrition in the human; a holy God does not experience contrition before another. OBS-030-045, OBS-030-062. |
| OBS-030-T2-143 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Contrition expresses the divine image indirectly — through its alignment with divine holiness. The contrite person is the one whose inner being has been aligned with God's own assessment of human moral condition. In this sense contrition is not the positive expression of a divine attribute in the human, but the human's truthful reception of divine reality. It expresses the image in its receptive mode: the image-bearer who accurately knows what they are before God. OBS-030-001, OBS-030-062. |
| OBS-030-T2-145 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | The presence of contrition reveals an image-bearer in truthful relation to their own creaturely condition — the person whose inner being is permeable to divine assessment. Absence of contrition (the hardened heart of Jer 44:10) reveals an image-bearer closed to this truth — self-sufficient, resistant to divine word. The hardened alternative is therefore an image-deficiency: the person who will not receive the divine verdict about their condition. OBS-030-028, OBS-030-047, OBS-030-062. |
| OBS-030-T2-151 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Contrition is primarily a settled inner-being condition — not an act, not a transient feeling, but a state the person inhabits. The adjectival vocabulary (dak.ka — "the contrite," na.kheh — "the crippled/contrite") designates a person characterised by this condition. However, contrition has a verbal history (the process of being crushed precedes the settled state) and can be refused (Jer 44:10), which means the will is implicated. It is best characterised as: a settled inner condition produced by encounter (with God, with moral reality) that the will can resist but not generate by autonomous decision. OBS-030-009, OBS-030-021, OBS-030-047. |
| OBS-030-T2-159 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | The verse evidence suggests speech accompanies contrition in the penitential context — Psa 51 is a spoken prayer, a vocal confession before God. The contrite posture issues in address to God ("be gracious to me," "create in me a clean heart"). However, the contrition vocabulary itself does not include a specific speech-act term; the speech dimension emerges from the verse context rather than being named in the characteristic's vocabulary. Isa 66:2's "trembling at my word" implies reception of divine speech rather than the contrite person's own speech-act. OBS-030-052, OBS-030-060. |
| OBS-030-T2-162 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | In the penitential mode, contrition sustained over time produces the settled character quality of lowliness — the absence of self-claim before God. Isa 66:2 presents the habitually humble and trembling person as the sustained product of ongoing orientation toward God's word. The settled adjectival forms (dak.ka, na.kheh) describe persons characterised by this condition over time. The sustained effect is not permanent brokenness but permanent lowliness of posture — openness to divine assessment as a character trait. OBS-030-009, OBS-030-017, OBS-030-021, OBS-030-060, OBS-030-061. |
| OBS-030-T2-163 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Sustained contrition establishes: (1) Lowliness as character quality — the ongoing posture of the person who makes no merit-claim before God (OBS-030-017). (2) Permeability to divine word — Isa 66:2 pairs contrition with trembling at God's word; sustained contrition produces openness to divine address as a stable character orientation (OBS-030-060, OBS-030-061). (3) Receptivity to divine reviving — the contrite person is the one whom God specifically looks to with reviving intent; sustained contrition keeps the person in this receptive position (OBS-030-046). *New finding: sustained contrition produces three inter-related character capacities — lowliness, word-permeability, and divine-reviving receptivity — that together constitute the contrite person's stable inner orientation.* OBS-030-017, OBS-030-046, OBS-030-060. |
| OBS-030-T2-165 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Three enabling conditions from Isa 66:2 — humility (lowly posture before God), contrition (crushed spirit — the condition itself names its own ground), and trembling at God's word (orientation toward divine speech). From the broader verse evidence: honest self-knowledge before God (the recognition of having caused actual harm, not surface shame — OBS-030-001); inner permeability rather than hardness (the opposite of Jer 44:10's hardened alternative — OBS-030-028). The enabling condition is fundamentally the absence of self-sufficiency — the openness of the inner being to divine assessment. OBS-030-001, OBS-030-028, OBS-030-060. |
| OBS-030-T2-169 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | The primary evidence: (1) The dominant group descriptions all frame contrition as the inner being before God in a posture of brokenness and dependence (Groups 7552-003, 7553-001, 7554-001, 7555-001, 7557-001). (2) The anchor verses in this dimension consistently name God as the one to whom the contrite person is exposed (Isa 57:15, Isa 66:2, Psa 34:18, Psa 51:17). (3) The characteristic produces reception of divine action rather than independent human achievement. OBS-030-022, OBS-030-045, OBS-030-048, OBS-030-052. |
| OBS-030-T2-171 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Isa 66:2 | Yes — explicitly. The contrition vocabulary is most consistently located in the spirit (*ruach*): "crushed in spirit" (Psa 34:18), "contrite and lowly spirit" (Isa 57:15), "humble and contrite in spirit" (Isa 66:2), "broken spirit" (Psa 51:17). The spirit is the primary named locus across the primary anchor verses. OBS-030-013, OBS-030-045, OBS-030-048, OBS-030-052, OBS-030-060. |
| OBS-030-T2-179 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Isa 66:2 | To the extent that cognitive self-knowledge underlies contrition (OBS-030-001), mind-location would reveal that contrition requires truthful self-assessment — the mind that accurately knows its own condition before God. This is partially evidenced from the registry description and from Isa 66:2's trembling at God's word (which involves cognitive reception of divine address). But explicit mind-vocabulary is absent from the anchor verses. Gap noted. OBS-030-001, OBS-030-060. |
| OBS-030-T2-190 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Contrition originates in the encounter between divine holiness and human moral condition — it is produced by relational encounter, not generated from within by autonomous human decision. The origin is constitutionally external to the self (divine holiness as the generative cause) but experienced internally (at the spirit and heart level). The passive grammar of the vocabulary (being crushed, being smitten) confirms the external origin. However, the will is implicated in whether the person remains open or hardens (Jer 44:10 — the refusal of contrition). OBS-030-007, OBS-030-045, OBS-030-047. |
| OBS-030-T2-195 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Yes — through the divine "looking" at the contrite. Isa 66:2: "this is the one to whom I will look." The divine seeing/attention is directed specifically at the contrite person. The perceptive engagement is asymmetric: God sees the contrite; the contrite is the object of divine perception. Whether the contrite person's own perception is engaged is partially evidenced — Isa 66:2's trembling at God's word implies perceptive reception of divine address. OBS-030-060, OBS-030-062. |
| OBS-030-T2-196 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Contrition deepens perceptive capacity in one specific direction: it opens the person to receive divine address (trembling at God's word — Isa 66:2). The contrite person is not closed to divine communication but particularly open to it. The hardened alternative (Jer 44:10 — not walking in God's law) implies perceptive closure to divine word. *New finding: contrition deepens the perceptive capacity for divine address — the contrite person is specifically receptive to God's word in a way the hardened person is not.* OBS-030-060, OBS-030-028. |
| OBS-030-T2-197 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | The pattern reveals contrition as a perceptive-opening event — the inner breaking simultaneously opens the person to divine address. The hardened heart is perceptively closed; the contrite heart is perceptively receptive. Contrition is the condition in which the perceptive faculty is most available to God's word and God's presence. OBS-030-028, OBS-030-060, OBS-030-062. |
| OBS-030-T2-198 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Yes — honest self-knowledge is named as the ground of genuine contrition: "not the surface shame of being caught but the interior grief of having actually caused harm or broken trust" (registry description). Contrition requires accurate cognitive assessment of one's own moral condition. Additionally, Isa 66:2's trembling at God's word implies cognitive reception and processing of divine address. OBS-030-001, OBS-030-060. |
| OBS-030-T2-199 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Contrition deepens self-cognition — it requires and produces honest self-knowledge. The contrite person cannot simultaneously maintain self-deception and genuine contrition; the inner-being breaking is partly the breaking of cognitive self-protection. The hardened alternative (Jer 44:10) is cognitively closed — the un-contrite person does not receive the divine word because cognitive closure prevents it. OBS-030-001, OBS-030-028, OBS-030-047. |
| OBS-030-T2-200 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Contrition is cognitively demanding — it requires the most honest self-assessment the inner being is capable of. The pattern reveals an inseparability of genuine contrition and accurate self-knowledge; counterfeit contrition (surface shame of being caught) is a cognitive failure, not merely an emotional one. OBS-030-001, OBS-030-003. |
| OBS-030-T2-207 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Yes — the will is implicated in whether contrition is received or refused. Jer 44:10 (the refusal of contrition) names volitional acts: "they have not humbled themselves" — a willed refusal. Isa 66:2 identifies the contrite person as one who trembles at God's word — an orientation that involves volitional submission to divine address. However, the origin of contrition is not primarily a volitional act — the person does not choose to be crushed. The will is present in the receiving or refusing, not in the generating. OBS-030-007, OBS-030-028, OBS-030-047, OBS-030-060. |
| OBS-030-T2-208 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Contrition redirects volition — the will of the contrite person is re-oriented toward God rather than toward self. The contrite person's volitional capacity is not destroyed but re-aimed: Psa 51:10 (in context — "create in me a clean heart") is a volitional request directed toward God. The contrite will is a willing-toward-God rather than a willing-for-self. OBS-030-052, OBS-030-055. |
| OBS-030-T2-209 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Volition is present in contrition but in a secondary, responsive mode — the will receives and confirms what the encounter with divine holiness has produced; it does not generate contrition autonomously. The pattern reveals contrition as a characteristic that re-orients rather than destroys the will. OBS-030-007, OBS-030-047. |
| OBS-030-T2-210 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Contrition engages agency asymmetrically. In its origin, contrition is passive — the person is acted upon (crushed, broken, smitten). In its expression, a secondary agency emerges: the contrite person prays (Psa 51), seeks God's face (Psa 34:18 — by implication), and in Isa 66:2 trembles at God's word — all agentive responses within the contrite posture. OBS-030-007, OBS-030-052, OBS-030-060. |
| OBS-030-T2-211 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Contrition transforms rather than destroys agency. The pre-contrite self-directed agency (the merit-claiming person approaching God on their own terms) is broken; the post-contrite agency is receptive and God-directed (seeking divine response rather than asserting self-sufficiency). *New finding: contrition converts self-directed agency into God-directed agency — the person stops acting for themselves and begins acting toward God in receptive dependence.* OBS-030-047, OBS-030-052, OBS-030-053. |
| OBS-030-T2-212 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | The agency pattern reveals contrition as a characteristic that humbles rather than eliminates agency. The contrite person remains an acting self but the direction of their action changes from self-assertion to God-seeking. OBS-030-052, OBS-030-060. |
| OBS-030-T2-219 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Yes — the three-fold posture of Isa 66:2 (humble + contrite + trembling at God's word) is a conscientious orientation: integrated moral awareness (humble), inner-being response (contrite), and action-alignment (trembling at and responding to God's word). Conscientiousness — the integrated moral-volitional-action response — is the stable character of the person shaped by contrition. OBS-030-060, OBS-030-061. |
| OBS-030-T2-220 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Contrition deepens conscientiousness by grounding it in honest moral self-knowledge rather than external performance. The contrite person who has genuinely received conscience's verdict develops a more integrated moral response — not rule-keeping as external compliance but genuine inner alignment. OBS-030-001, OBS-030-052, OBS-030-060. |
| OBS-030-T2-221 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Contrition grounds conscientiousness in inner reality rather than external performance — it makes the integrated moral-volitional-action response genuine rather than formal. OBS-030-001, OBS-030-052. |
| OBS-030-T2-222 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Yes — contrition is primarily relational in its penitential mode: the inner being before God. The divine-human relational dynamic is what contrition opens: God draws near (Psa 34:18), God dwells with (Isa 57:15), God looks to (Isa 66:2). The contrite posture is the inner posture that enables divine-human relational proximity. OBS-030-045, OBS-030-048, OBS-030-062. |
| OBS-030-T2-224 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Contrition is the relational capacity-enabler for divine nearness — it is the inner opening through which divine-human proximity becomes possible after moral failure. The pattern reveals contrition as constitutively relational: it exists for the sake of the divine-human encounter. OBS-030-045, OBS-030-048, OBS-030-062. |
| OBS-030-T2-225 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Isa 66:2 | Yes — and this is the primary relational direction. God draws near the brokenhearted (Psa 34:18), God dwells with the contrite spirit (Isa 57:15), God looks to the humble and contrite (Isa 66:2), God does not despise the broken spirit (Psa 51:17). In every primary anchor verse, God's relational movement is toward the contrite person. OBS-030-045, OBS-030-048, OBS-030-052, OBS-030-062. |
| OBS-030-T2-227 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Isa 66:2 | God's consistent drawing near to the contrite reveals a divine disposition of particular attentiveness to the broken inner being. The divine gaze (Isa 66:2 — "to whom I will look") is directed specifically at the humble and contrite — not at the successful or the ritually compliant. This reveals that divine favour is not attracted by human strength but by human openness in weakness. OBS-030-062. |
| OBS-030-T2-228 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Isa 66:2 | Yes — the penitential mode is precisely the human movement toward God through contrition. The contrite person's posture (lowly spirit, humble, trembling at God's word) is a movement toward God-available-space. Psa 51 is the definitive human-to-God contrite movement — the entire psalm is a contrite approach to God following moral failure. OBS-030-052, OBS-030-060. |
| OBS-030-T2-229 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Isa 66:2's three-fold posture: humble, contrite in spirit, trembling at God's word. The inner posture required is: (1) lowliness — no self-elevation; (2) crushed spirit — the inner being not hardened; (3) word-permeability — openness to divine address. These three together constitute the inner posture for genuine human-to-God contrite movement. OBS-030-060, OBS-030-061. |
| OBS-030-T2-244 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | The mechanism is encounter-induced dissolution: the inner being's encounter with divine holiness (or adversarial force, or moral reality) dissolves its self-protective structures, producing the contrite state. The change mechanism is not discipline (gradual formation), not sudden dramatic transformation, but the dissolution of inner resistance through confrontation with a reality the person cannot deflect. *New finding: contrition's change mechanism is dissolution-through-encounter — the inner being's self-enclosure is broken by a reality it cannot absorb without being changed.* OBS-030-007, OBS-030-045, OBS-030-062. |
| OBS-030-T2-248 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Yes — the settled character of lowliness produced by contrition (Isa 66:2 — the habitually humble and trembling person) is a character formed over time through the repeated experience of encountering divine holiness and being opened by it. Isa 57:15's reviving of spirit and heart is a formative event — it produces inner change that shapes subsequent character. OBS-030-017, OBS-030-060, OBS-030-061. |
| OBS-030-T2-249 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Contrition functions as the recurring inner reset in the sanctification arc — the event that prevents the accumulation of pride and self-sufficiency by returning the person to the posture of lowliness before God. The settled character of Isa 66:2 (habitually humble, contrite, word-trembling) is the product of contrition repeated over time, not of a single episode. OBS-030-017, OBS-030-060. |
| OBS-030-T2-253 | CROSS_REGISTRY | Isa 66:2 | From the v1 obslog §G co-occurrence data: R183 (heart) — 6 shared verses (strongest signal); R061 (fear) — 2 shared anchors; R123 (pride) — 3 shared verses including 1 shared anchor; R151 (sorrow) — 1 shared anchor; R062 (fellowship) — 1 shared anchor. The top co-occurrence registries reflect the inner posture cluster (heart), the companion characteristic cluster (fear, trembling), and the structural opposite cluster (pride). OBS-030-030, OBS-030-032, OBS-030-033, OBS-030-034. |
| OBS-030-T2-254 | CROSS_REGISTRY | Isa 66:2 | The co-occurrence pattern reveals contrition as a convergence characteristic — it consistently appears at the intersection of multiple inner-being registers: heart (the moral-evaluative centre), fear (the companion affective posture), and pride (the structural opposite). Contrition does not sit in isolation but at a nexus where several characteristics meet in the same verses. *New finding: contrition occupies a convergence position in the inner-being landscape — it consistently appears where heart, fear, and pride-dynamics are all active simultaneously.* OBS-030-030, OBS-030-033, OBS-030-034. |
| OBS-030-T2-258 | CROSS_REGISTRY | Isa 66:2 | Contrition is produced by the encounter with divine holiness — which is not itself a characteristic in the inner-being registry sense but the divine reality that acts as causal agent. At the characteristic level, the verse evidence implies that fear of God (R061) is a companion-cause — Isa 66:2 pairs contrition with trembling at God's word, suggesting that God-fearing orientation is both companion to and possibly productive of contrition. SD003 captures this question. OBS-030-033, OBS-030-060. |
| OBS-030-T2-275 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Yes — H1793A (dak.ka — "the contrite one") and H5223 (na.kheh — "the contrite/crippled one") are adjectival person-type terms that designate the person characterised by contrition. Isa 57:15 ("I dwell with the contrite") and Isa 66:2 ("the humble and contrite one") use these in person-type designations. OBS-030-009, OBS-030-021. |
| OBS-030-T2-280 | VERSE_ANNOTATION | Isa 66:2 | The primary evidence is carried by psalm (Psa 51, Psa 34, Psa 143) and prophecy (Isa 53, Isa 57, Isa 66, Jer 44, Jer 46). The psalm genre shapes interpretation: penitential psalms present contrition in the context of direct address to God — the inner posture is expressed as prayer. The prophetic genre shapes interpretation differently: Isaiah's contrition verses are divine address (God speaks about the one he dwells with), not human prayer. Both forms are present, requiring distinct interpretive approaches. OBS-030-052, OBS-030-045, OBS-030-060. |
| OBS-030-T2-282 | VERSE_ANNOTATION | Isa 66:2 | Primary settings: (1) Penitential/liturgical — Psa 51 (individual penitential psalm in the context of specific moral failure); (2) Prophetic-covenantal — Isa 57:15 and 66:2 (divine address within prophetic warning/promise sequence); (3) Lament — Psa 34:18 (hymn of thanksgiving arising from distress); (4) Servant Song — Isa 53:5 (prophetic servant poetry with cultic-sacrificial overtones). The settings require contextually sensitive reading: the penitential psalm is personal and confessional; the prophetic address is community-directed. OBS-030-045, OBS-030-048, OBS-030-052, OBS-030-060. |
| OBS-030-T2-287 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | The verse evidence presents contrition as arising in divine-human encounter — a relational event with a holy God as the causative agent. Human science frameworks (moral psychology) frame guilt as arising from internal moral standards and social internalization — without requiring a divine agent. The divergence reveals that biblical contrition has a theocentric causality that purely human-science accounts of moral emotion cannot accommodate. The framework maps the inner-being phenomenology but cannot explain the causative structure. OBS-030-045, OBS-030-062. |
| OBS-030-T2-288 | OBSERVATION | Isa 66:2 | Developmental psychology raises the question of how contrition is formed in the person over time — what sequence of formative experiences produces the habitually lowly and contrite character of Isa 66:2. This is partially evidenced (the verse evidence confirms the settled character exists) but the developmental pathway is not named in the verse evidence. Whether there are developmentally predictable patterns to how a person acquires habitual contrition is a genuine gap. OBS-030-017, OBS-030-060. |

**Findings — direct (Strong's mention) (0)**

(none)

**Findings — via anchor verse (6 unique)**

| Finding ID | Type | Matched anchor refs | Excerpt |
|---|---|---|---|
| OBS-117-T2-040 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Joh 14:27 | Yes — with rich evidence. Key heart locations: (1) Deu 29:19 (2509-002 anchor, OBS-117-150) — "blesses himself in his heart [lev]" claiming shalom while walking in "stubbornness of my heart" — false peace is a heart-generated claim; the heart is the seat of the false shalom; (2) 1Ch 12:17 (2510-001 anchor, OBS-117-151) — "my heart will be joined to you" — the shalom of friendship is a heart-bond; (3) Joh 14:27 — "Let not your hearts [kardia] be troubled" — Christ's peace addresses the heart directly; the troubled heart and the peace are antithetical (G1515 426-001 anchor, prior session OBS-117-120); (4) Phili 4:7 — "the peace of God... will guard your hearts [kardia] and your minds" — the heart is the primary guarded territory; (5) Pro 12:20 — "those who plan peace have joy" — planning peace is a heart-act (prior session OBS-117-096 noted the heart-disposition of planning); (6) Psa 28:3 — "speak peace with their neighbors while evil is in their hearts" — heart as the locus of authentic or false orientation toward peace. The data shows 33 co-occurring verses with R183 (heart) — the highest co-occurrence count in the entire registry (G.2, OBS-117-016). |
| OBS-117-T2-041 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Joh 14:27 | The heart-location of peace engages all four of the heart's integrating functions: (1) Knowing (cognitive): Rom 8:6 ("to set the mind/heart on the Spirit is life and peace") — the heart's cognitive orientation toward God produces peace; the directed heart knows what produces peace; (2) Willing (volitional): Psa 120:7 ("I am for peace") — the heart's volitional orientation toward peace as identity; Isa 30:15 ("but you were unwilling") — the refusal of peace is a heart-act of will; (3) Feeling (affective): Joh 14:27 ("let not your hearts be troubled") — the troubled heart as the experiential opposite of peace; the heart as the seat of distress or rest; (4) Moral awareness (conscience): Deu 29:19 — the heart's stubbornness as the moral condition that generates false shalom; Psa 28:3 — evil in the heart contrasted with speaking peace. The heart is the integrating centre of peace's constitutional address: peace must be received, held, directed, and expressed from the heart. The heart-peace connection is the most comprehensive single-location engagement in the data. |
| OBS-117-T2-053 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Joh 14:27 | The data establishes a primary origin and two secondary origins: (1) Primary — bestowed by God: the overwhelming weight of the evidence shows shalom as divine gift. The Aaronic blessing (Num 6:26 — "the Lord... give you peace"), God's covenant of peace (Isa 54:10), God speaking peace to his saints (Psa 85:8), God planning welfare (Jer 29:11), Christ as the peace-giver (Joh 14:27 — "my peace I give to you"), Spirit-fruit peace (Gal 5:22) — all establish God as the constitutional source. The human person cannot generate authentic shalom from within. (2) Secondary — formed from within through orientation: Isa 26:3 — the mind stayed on God produces perfect peace; the person's own cognitive act of orientation enables the reception of what God provides. This is not generation from within but reception through orientation; (3) Generated falsely from within: the false-shalom pattern (Deu 29:19, Jer 6:14) — the person can generate a counterfeit inner condition of peace by self-deception or false claim, but this is precisely what the data condemns. Authentic constitutional origin: divine gift received through trust and covenant orientation. |
| OBS-117-T2-054 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Joh 14:27 | The origin is singular in ground but multiple in mechanism. Ground: God alone is the ultimate source — whether through covenant (2508-002), through Christ (426-001, Eph 2:14), or through the Spirit (Gal 5:22), all peace traces back to God as its constitutional source. Mechanism: three distinct modes of origination appear in the data: (1) Covenantal gift — God gives shalom through covenant (Num 6:26, Isa 54:10); the covenant is the structural channel; (2) Christological accomplishment — peace purchased through the cross (Isa 53:5, Col 1:20, G1517 430-001); Christ's act constitutes the peace; (3) Pneumatological formation — peace formed as Spirit-fruit (Gal 5:22); the Spirit produces peace over time within the person. These three mechanisms correspond to the three persons of the Trinity — the origin is Trinitarian in structure, though the data does not use that language explicitly. The singular ground (God) and multiple mechanisms prevent both monism (peace from only one channel) and pluralism (peace from multiple independent sources). |
| OBS-117-T2-088 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Joh 14:27 | Yes — this is the dominant direction in the peace corpus. The God-to-human operation is extensively documented: (1) Covenant gift: Num 6:26 ("the Lord give you peace" — Aaronic blessing), Isa 54:10 ("my covenant of peace shall not be removed"), Jer 29:11 ("plans for welfare and not for evil"); (2) God speaking peace: Psa 85:8 ("he will speak peace to his people, to his saints"); (3) Christ-given peace: Joh 14:27 ("my peace I give to you"); (4) Spirit-given peace: Gal 5:22 (Spirit-fruit); (5) God making well-being: Isa 45:7 ("I make well-being"); (6) The God of peace: Rom 15:33, 16:20, Phili 4:9, 1Th 5:23 — God's identity as "the God of peace" who acts toward the human person. The God-to-human direction is established at every level: covenant, speech, person of Christ, Spirit, and title. |
| OBS-117-T2-089 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Joh 14:27 | The data establishes covenant as the primary basis. God's peace is extended: (1) Through covenant: Num 25:12 ("my covenant of peace"), Isa 54:10 (covenant of peace that shall not be removed), Eze 34:25, 37:26 (covenants of peace in the new covenant context); (2) Through covenant faithfulness: Psa 85:8 — God speaks peace to his saints "but let them not turn back to folly" — the condition is covenant fidelity, not merit; (3) Through the cross: Col 1:20 ("making peace by the blood of his cross") — the basis shifts in the NT from the Sinai covenant to the new covenant accomplished in Christ's sacrifice; (4) Through grace not merit: Joh 14:27 ("not as the world gives do I give to you") — the basis of Christ's peace-gift is explicitly distinguished from transactional exchange; the gift is given freely. The ground shifts from covenant-as-obligation to covenant-as-grace across the canon. |

**Findings — via anchor verse (9 unique)**

| Finding ID | Type | Matched anchor refs | Excerpt |
|---|---|---|---|
| OBS-117-T2-024 | SOMATIC_EVIDENCE | Deu 28:65 | Documented immediate responses to shalom's absence: (1) Soul bereft — Lam 3:17 ("my soul is bereft of peace; I have forgotten what happiness is") — total inner destitution, loss of access to happiness itself; (2) Bones wasting — Psa 32:3 (prior session: "when I kept silent, my bones wasted away through my groaning all day long") — somatic deterioration; (3) Trembling heart — Deu 28:65 ("a trembling heart and failing eyes and a languishing soul") — the triple somatic-inner expression of peacelessness in judgment; (4) Anguish seeking — Eze 7:25 ("when anguish comes they will seek peace, but there shall be none"); (5) Job's triple negation — Job 3:26 ("I am not at ease, nor am I quiet... I have no rest, but trouble comes"). The withdrawal of shalom is experienced as total inner collapse — not discomfort but destitution. The soul's access to its own capacity for happiness is severed (Lam 3:17). |
| OBS-117-T2-027 | SOMATIC_EVIDENCE | Deu 28:65 | Sustained absence of shalom produces progressive deterioration: (1) Somatic degradation — Psa 38:3 ("no soundness in my flesh... no health in my bones because of my sin") — sustained peacelessness shows in the body; (2) Exile and homelessness — Deu 28:65 ("you shall find no respite, and there shall be no resting place for the sole of your foot") — sustained peacelessness produces the ultimate displacement; (3) Universal desolation — Jer 12:12 ("no flesh has peace") — when shalom is withdrawn from a community, the deprivation becomes total; (4) The wicked's false prosperity — Job 21:9 ("their houses are safe from fear") reveals by contrast: the wicked have external safety but not genuine shalom — the sustained absence of authentic peace produces the counterfeit of complacent ease. The trajectory: inner → somatic → communal → eschatological. |
| OBS-117-T2-046 | SOMATIC_EVIDENCE | Deu 28:65 | Yes — and this is one of the most extensive somatic evidence sets in the programme. Multiple body parts explicitly linked to peace's presence or absence: (1) Bones (etsem): Psa 32:3 ("my bones wasted away through my groaning all day long") — withheld confession/peace produces bone deterioration; Psa 38:3 ("there is no health [shalom] in my bones because of my sin") — OBS-117-149; shalom named as the soundness-of-bones; (2) Flesh (basar): Psa 38:3 ("there is no soundness in my flesh because of your indignation") — flesh linked to peace-as-soundness; (3) Eyes: Deu 28:65 ("failing eyes") — peacelessness in judgment produces ocular failure; (4) Feet/sole: Deu 28:65 ("no resting place for the sole of your foot") — the body's connection to the land as peace's somatic expression; (5) Inward parts/belly (meah): Job 30:27 — OBS-117-066; (6) Body-sleep (Psa 4:8) — the whole body at rest as the expression of peace ("I will both lie down and sleep"); (7) Wounds (Isa 53:5 — "with his wounds we are healed") — the Servant's body as the instrument of peace's purchase. |
| OBS-117-T2-047 | SOMATIC_EVIDENCE | Deu 28:65 | The body-part links serve multiple functions: (1) Indicative — the body's condition indicates the inner-being condition: Psa 38:3 (no soundness in flesh/no health in bones because of sin) — the body reads out the inner state of peacelessness; the body is a diagnostic display of the inner condition; (2) Emphatic — Deu 28:65 accumulates three somatic signals (trembling heart, failing eyes, languishing soul) to intensify the portrait of peacelessness in judgment; the body amplifies the inner condition; (3) Expressive — Psa 4:8 (lying down and sleeping) — the body enacts peace by doing what peace enables; sleep is the body's expression of inner security; (4) Mediating — Isa 53:5 ("with his wounds we are healed") — the Servant's body mediates peace to others; the physical wounds are the mechanism of the relational restoration. The most significant body-link is Psa 38:3: the explicit naming of shalom as soundness-of-bones under sin's influence establishes that inner peace and somatic integrity are structurally connected — not metaphorically but causally. |
| OBS-117-T2-055 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Deu 28:65 | Yes — and this is the most analytically significant T2 finding for the peace registry. The constitutional movement of peace is extensively documented, operating in multiple directions: (1) Spirit → soul → body (downward cascade under loss of peace): The absence of peace radiates from the inner person outward: Deu 28:65 — peacelessness produces trembling heart (volitional/heart level) + failing eyes (body level) + languishing soul (soul level); Psa 32:3 — suppressed inner condition → bones wasting (body); Psa 38:3 — sin disrupting inner peace → no soundness in flesh, no health in bones. The movement under un-peace: inner disorder → somatic deterioration. (2) God → spirit → soul → body (downward cascade under the gift of peace): Gal 5:22 (Spirit produces peace as fruit) → Phili 4:7 (peace guards hearts and minds) → Psa 4:8 (peace enables the body to lie down and sleep). The gift moves from its divine source through the spirit/Spirit level into the heart and mind, and from there into somatic rest. (3) Body → inner (the redemptive reversal): Isa 53:5 — the Servant's wounded body → peace received in others' inner being; the movement against the normal direction, accomplished through the cross. |
| OBS-117-T2-057 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Deu 28:65 | Yes — peace engages perception primarily in its negative form: the perceptive faculty is disturbed, dulled, or altered when peace is absent. Evidence: (1) Deu 28:65 — "failing eyes" as a somatic expression of peacelessness; the eyes (a perceptive organ) fail under the condition of un-peace in judgment; (2) The silence vocabulary in this registry (H1827 demamah, G4602 sigē) names the threshold-quiet before perception of the divine voice — 1Ki 19:12 (still small voice after the demamah-silence), OBS-117-069 from prior session; the silence that is peace's companion is precisely the condition that enables divine perception; (3) Psa 131:2 — "I have calmed and quieted my soul... like a weaned child" — the quieted soul is positioned for receptive perception; restlessness prevents this. |
| OBS-117-T2-058 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Deu 28:65 | Peace enables perception — specifically, the silence/stillness dimension of peace enables the perception of the divine voice and divine reality. The pattern: demamah (profound silence, H1827) is the threshold before divine speech (1Ki 19:12, Job 4:16 — prior session OBS-117-069, 070); the quieted soul is receptive; the restless soul cannot hear what silence carries. Conversely, the absence of peace impairs perception — "failing eyes" (Deu 28:65) is the somatic expression. The mechanism: peace as stillness creates the condition for perception; restlessness as noise prevents it. This is the hearing-direction of the silence vocabulary: peace enables the person to be still enough to perceive God. |
| OBS-117-T2-074 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Deu 28:65 | Peace enables agency — the peaceful person is constitutionally equipped to act in the world from a stable inner base rather than from reactive anxiety. Evidence: (1) Dan 10:19 — "peace be with you; be strong and of good courage" — the angelic peace-gift produces strength and courage for action; peace precedes and enables Daniel's capacity to act on the vision; (2) Isa 32:17 — "the effect of righteousness will be peace, and the result of righteousness, quietness and trust forever" — the peace condition produces trust, which is the basis for courageous action; (3) Deu 28:65 reverse — the absence of peace produces the "trembling heart" and "languishing soul" that impair agency; fearful and anxious people cannot act decisively. Conversely: complacent ease (H7600 group 413-001) impairs agency by producing false security and contempt for consequences — a corrupted form of "peace" that disengages agency. |
| OBS-117-T2-128 | OBSERVATION | Deu 28:65 | The closest neighbours requiring distinction work: (1) Rest (nuach/menuchah — major component of R117 itself): rest and peace co-reside in this registry, which creates an internal distinction challenge. Rest is the cessation-of-striving dimension; peace is the positive wholeness-condition that rest may produce or accompany. Rest can be given and withdrawn (Deu 28:65 — no resting place); peace encompasses more than the cessation of striving (shalom includes welfare, friendship, covenant, and messianic embodiment). Rest is a component of peace's semantic range but not co-extensive with it; (2) Joy (R97, 21 shared verses): joy and peace are frequently paired (Gal 5:22 — adjacent Spirit-fruits; Isa 55:12 — "go out in joy... led forth in peace"). Joy is the positive affective response; peace is the positive existential condition. Joy can be present without complete peace (James 1:2 — "count it all joy... when you meet trials of various kinds" — joy in trials doesn't require peaceful resolution); peace at its fullest produces joy but is not joy itself. Gap: the boundary between peace and rest (as internal to R117) requires Session D clarity — is rest a dimension of peace or a distinct characteristic captured by the same registry? |

(none)

<a id="s4"></a>
## §4. Appendix — items linked at registry or collection level

<a id="s4-1"></a>
### §4.1 Findings from contributor registries with no term-level link (8)

These findings sit on a registry that contributes terms to this cluster, but their text and anchor verses don't resolve to any specific cluster term. Candidates for term-level enrichment.

| Finding ID | Type | Registry | Anchor verses | Excerpt |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| DIM-001-001 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | R001 abomination |  | The new covenant transformation group (3272-001: diatithēmi — the covenantal act writing divine law on the inner mind and heart) appears in the abomination registry. This places the new covenant's inner transformation as the divine answer to abomination and inner defilement. Session B should examine whether the abomination cluster's verse evidence shows the new covenant specifically as the remedy for abomination — and whether this pattern recurs across the cluster. |
| DIM-4-001 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | R004 anger |  | Anger governance is the paradigmatic inner-being governance challenge in Reg 4. Groups 79-004 (mastery of anger exceeds military conquest), 1554-001 (trembling restraint before God without sin), 38-001 (morally accountable anger under divine command), and 139-003 (wisdom counsel not to let anger kindle) show anger mastery as a distinct and critical sub-theme. Session B should map the vocabulary of anger-governance as a structured inner-being claim about will, character, and spiritual posture. |
| DIM-4-002 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | R004 anger |  | Two groups (1552-001: fierce anger co-existing with grief/loyalty; 37-003: righteous anger co-existing with sorrow at hardness of heart) show the inner being holding anger and love, or anger and grief, simultaneously as genuine compound affective states. Session B should examine whether Scripture treats compound anger-with-grief as a distinct inner-being mode and what theological conditions produce it. |
| DIM-005-001 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | R005 anguish |  | Group 4667-002 (H7114A qa.tser, be short — divine yielding): assigned Theological/Divine-Human. This group names divine pathos — God himself moved by the misery of his people. It is one of the clearest instances in the anguish registry of Scripture attributing an inner affective response to God. Session B should note this as a significant theological dimension within Registry 5 and consider its relationship to the broader divine-pathos theme across C05. |
| DIM-7-001 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | R007 anxiety |  | merimnaō (G3309) operates in two distinct inner-being registers: anxious affective worry (2709-001, 2709-002) and volitional-attentional directed care (2709-003, 350-001). Session B should map how the same word spans these two registers and what this reveals about anxiety as both an affective state and a directional inner-being act. |
| DIM-051-001 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | R051 distress |  | H7379 (riv, strife/contention) has 2 healthy active groups in distress (#51): 234-001 (strife/contention, 19 verses) and 234-002 (pleading one's cause, 26 verses). A third group was created for the indictment/controversy sense — God's legal case against his people in the prophetic tradition — but was never populated with verse_context records and has been delete_flagged. Session B analyst should assess whether this prophetic lawsuit dimension of H7379 belongs within distress and whether the verse evidence warrants a third group. Candidate verses would be found in prophetic lawsuit texts (Isaiah, Jeremiah, Micah) where H7379 names God's formal contention with Israel. |
| DIM-051-002 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | R051 distress |  | Group 235-002 (H7451A ra, harmful spirit afflicting Saul): assigned Theological/Divine-Human. This group sits on the boundary between demonological, psychological, and theological dimensions — the harmful spirit is theologically constituted (sent by God per 1 Sam 16) but produces what functions as an inner-psychological affliction. The existing dimension vocabulary may be inadequate to name this precisely. Session B should examine the verse evidence and consider whether a note on the vocabulary gap is warranted. |
| DIM-051-003 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | R051 distress |  | Registry 51 (distress) contains a significant cluster of outlier groups arriving via XREF terms that are outside the suffering domain: 242-001 (meditation/contemplation, Cognitive/Mind), 3600-001 (divine forming of the inner person, Theological/Divine-Human), 5129-002 (opened ear as inner receptivity, Spiritual/God-ward), 5168-001 (embrace as expression of fulfilment, Affective/Emotional), 5124-001 and 5126-001 (amazement/astonishment). These should be treated as peripheral in Session B analysis of Registry 51 and may warrant a vocabulary or cluster note. |

<a id="s4-2"></a>
### §4.2 SD pointers from contributor registries with no term-level link (12)

| Pointer | Priority | Strong's ref | Description |
|---|---|---|---|
| DIM-001-SD001 | MEDIUM |  | The new covenant transformation group (3272-001) appears in the abomination registry and salvation vocabulary groups appear in the debauchery registry (Reg 39) — both placing redemptive vocabulary within moral-failure/defilement registries through the XREF mechanism. Session D should examine whether this is a programme-wide pattern: are there other clusters where redemptive/salvation vocabulary appears in moral-failure registries via XREF, and what does this reveal about the inner-being logic connecting defilement and redemption in Scripture? |
| SP-067-006 | HIGH |  | Eze 36:31 is a shared anchor between R67 (Group 884-006 — not-good moral verdict) and R1 (abomination). The verse places recognition of deeds as not-good alongside 'iniquities and abominations' — self-loathing for the latter follows from recognition of the former. Session D should examine: (a) whether the not-good and abomination registers share an inner-being mechanism (both produce self-directed moral revulsion); (b) whether Eze 36:31 establishes a causal chain from not-good recognition to self-loathing that connects R67 and R1; and (c) whether Rom 2:4 (divine chreestotees leads to repentance) extends this sequence to a goodness-abomination-repentance arc. |
| DIM-111-SD005 | MEDIUM |  | H5750 od names sustained divine dispositions in opposite directions: mercy endures (Hab 2:3); anger stretched out still (Isa 5:25). Do mercy and wrath share persistence structure as expressions of divine faithfulness? Session D. |
| DIM-023-SD019 | HIGH |  | Isa 54:8 — moment of anger vs everlasting chesed/racham — establishes a temporal asymmetry in divine inner-being: judgment is temporary, compassion is permanent. This directly addresses the question of which divine characteristic is more fundamental. Cross-registry: Anger (Reg 4), Love (Reg 103). The verse is a candidate for the C17 cluster synthesis anchor verse. *G4697 splanchnizō — Mar 1:41 (non-anchor, somatic) "Moved with pity, he stretched out his hand and touched him." The compassion movement (splanchnizō*) is immediately followed by physical touch — Jesus reaches out and touches a leper (socially and ritually untouchable). The inner movement produces a boundary-crossing bodily act. This is the most direct example in the corpus of visceral compassion producing physical contact. |
| DIM-023-SD026 | MEDIUM |  | 2 shared anchor verses with Anger (Reg 4). Isa 54:8 names the temporal contrast between a moment of anger and everlasting chesed/racham (SD-019 already raised). The shared anchor with Anger confirms this is not an incidental pairing — the inner-being boundary between anger and compassion in the divine character is structurally significant. Cross-registry: Anger (Reg 4). Already partially covered by SD-019. |
| SP-067-008 | MEDIUM |  | Pro 16:32 ('slow to anger is better than the mighty; rules his spirit than takes a city') is a shared anchor with R4 (anger) and R199 (dominion/self-mastery). The verse uses the comparative wisdom framework (R67 Group 884-004) to assert that anger restraint and self-rule are of greater value than external power. Session D should examine whether this verse establishes a programme-level hierarchy of inner-being characteristics where self-regulation (slow to anger, ruling the spirit) is superior to external achievement — and whether this hierarchy is structural across wisdom literature or specific to this verse. |
| SP-067-015 | MEDIUM |  | Pro 16:32 ('slow to anger is better than the mighty; rules his spirit than takes a city') is a shared anchor with R4 (anger) and R199 (dominion/self-mastery). The verse is the anchor for Group 884-004 (comparative wisdom) and names anger restraint and self-rule as inner-being characteristics whose goodness (better-than value) exceeds external power. Session D should examine whether Pro 16:32 establishes a programme-wide hierarchy where self-regulation characteristics (anger restraint, self-rule) are structurally superior to external achievement — and whether this hierarchy is consistent across wisdom literature registries. Source: OBS-067-OBS-032. |
| DIM-11-SD001 | MEDIUM |  | The commanded-inner-state pattern — Scripture commanding specific inner orientations (do not be dismayed / fear the Lord / rejoice always) — appears across Registries 11, 97, 42 and likely others. Session D should trace this pattern across clusters and examine its implications for understanding the inner being as subject to divine instruction. |
| DIM-42-SD003 | HIGH |  | Two groups name the inner life as designed toward an end: 378-002 (chara — joy as the goal/completion of the inner life in God) and 6701-001 (miph.la.ah — wondrous works designed to evoke wonder). Researcher note: this may also include what God intends as the inner state of the person. These groups point toward a dimension the existing vocabulary does not name — the inner life as oriented toward a divinely intended goal. Session D should examine whether a new vocabulary category is needed. |
| 182-SD003 | MEDIUM | G5590H | Mat 10:28 — soul introduced as dimension surviving bodily death in fear context. Soul and fear registries share verse at the intersection of ultimate threat and ultimate protection. |
| DIM-61-SD001 | MEDIUM |  | C06 fear cluster shows a tripartite dimension pattern: fear-as-God-ward-orientation (Spiritual/God-ward ~18 groups), fear-as-inner-affect (Affective/Emotional ~37 groups), fear-as-volitional-collapse (Volitional/Will 5 groups). This tripartite structure — orientation, affect, will-collapse — may be a cross-registry finding about how negative inner states operate in biblical anthropology. Session D should examine whether the same pattern appears in other C06 registries and beyond. |
| DIM-33-SD001 | MEDIUM |  | Groups 763-001 and 763-002 (tharseō — divine 'Take heart/be courageous' address) in Reg 33 mirror the 'Fear not' pattern from Reg 61 (ya.re) in C06. The divine address directly to the inner being producing courage where there was fear is a structured biblical motif crossing C06 and C08. Session D should examine the divine courage-address as a cross-cluster pattern: how God's direct speech to the inner being (commanding against fear, commanding toward courage) functions as a distinctive inner-being transformation mechanism. |

<a id="s4-5"></a>
### §4.5 Cross-cluster orphan findings/pointers

Findings + SD pointers that mention M-cluster vocabulary but originate from registries that do NOT contribute terms to this cluster — see [wa-cluster-m01-finding-orphans-v1-…](../../../outputs/markdown/) for the full scan.
